Father's Khul' of Minor Daughter: The Guarantor Condition
Ruling on father's khul' of minor daughter with guarantor condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a father's khul' of his minor daughter is valid despite the minor's inability to be liable, and identify the condition for the divorce to take effect.

Core Idea
A father's khul' of his minor daughter is valid because the divorce is tied to his acceptance, not the daughter's liability.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the father's authority to effect khul' on behalf of his minor daughter. While some argued that the khul' cannot be valid because it depends on a financial obligation that a minor cannot bear, the soundest opinion (al-ashah) clarifies that the divorce is conditioned upon the father's acceptance, not the daughter's liability. We will unpack the reasoning, the role of the father as guarantor (damin), and the distinction between suretyship (kafalah) and guarantee (daman).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling according to the soundest opinion: the father's khul' of his minor daughter is valid (sahih) if the father acts as guarantor (damin) for the compensation. The divorce takes effect upon his acceptance.
The father must pay the compensation, but the daughter retains her right to dower (mahr).
2
Identify the Opposing View
Some Hanafi scholars said the divorce does not occur because the khul' is suspended on the obligation of payment (badal), and since the minor cannot be liable, the condition is impossible, so the divorce should not happen.
This view is mentioned in the text as the opinion that 'it was said that divorce does not occur'.
3
Analyse the Proof for the Soundest Opinion
The soundest opinion argues that the divorce is suspended on the father's acceptance, not on the minor's liability. The father's acceptance is a valid act of guardianship, so the divorce occurs.
The text cites al-Baraziyya as a source for this reasoning.
4
Understand the Father's Role as Damin
The father is a guarantor (damin) who undertakes to pay the compensation. This differs from kafalah (suretyship) because there is no primary debtor; the father is directly liable.
The text clarifies: 'it does not mean suretyship (kafalah), because there is no claim here against the original party at all.'
5
Examine the Condition on the Minor
If the compensation is stipulated on the minor herself, the divorce is suspended on her own acceptance (if she is capable). If she accepts, divorce occurs but she owes nothing because she is not subject to financial liability (gharamah). If the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations.
This shows the careful distinction between liability and the condition for divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في الأصح فإن خلعها على أنه ضامن صح، وعليه المال، وإن شرط المال عليها تطلق بلا شيء إن قبلت

قوله: في الأصح؛ مقابلة ما قيل أنه لا يقع الطلاق؛ لأنه معلق بلزوم المال، وإذ لم يلزم لا يقع، ووجه الأصح أنه معلق بقبول الأب من صغيرته، وقد وجد، فيقع الطلاق. كذا في «البرازية».

قوله: على أنه ضامن؛ أي ملتزم لأداء بدل الخلع، وليس المراد به الكفالة، فإنه كما يأتي في موضوعه عبارة عن ضم الذمة إلى الذمة في المطالبة، ولا مطالبة هاهنا على الأصيل مطلقاً.

قوله: وعليه؛ أي يجب على الأب المال، وهو بدل الخلع، لكن لا يسقط المهر؛ إذ لا ولاية عليها للأب في مثله، فإن كان الخلع على المهر فلها أن ترجع به على الزوج، ويرجع الزوج به على الأب لضمانه، ولو كان على غيره كالألف مثلاً ترجع بمهرها على الزوج، ولا يرجع الزوج به على الأب؛ لأنه لم يضمن له المهر بل الألف فقط. كذا في «النهر».

قوله: وإن شرط؛ أي إن شرط الزوج على الصغيرة، قال في «الهداية»: «إن شرط الألف عليها توقف على قبولها إن كانت من أهل القبول، فإن قبلت وقع الطلاق لوجود الشرط، ولا يجب المال؛ لأنها ليست من أهل الغرامة، فإن قبله الأب عنها ففيه روايتان».

انتهى من الهداية.
In the soundest opinion, if he made khul' with her on condition that he is a guarantor, it is valid, and the payment is upon him. If the payment is stipulated upon her, she is divorced with nothing upon her if she accepts.

He says: "In the soundest opinion" — contrary to what was said that divorce does not occur because it is suspended on the obligation of payment, and since payment is not required, it does not occur. The proof of the soundest opinion is that it is suspended on the acceptance of the father for his minor daughter, and that acceptance has occurred, so divorce occurs. Thus in al-Baraziyya.

He says: "On condition that he is a guarantor" — meaning he undertakes to pay the khul' compensation; it does not mean suretyship (kafalah), because as will come in its topic, that is the addition of one liability to another in seeking payment, and there is no claim here against the original party at all.

He says: "And the payment is upon him" — meaning the father must pay the khul' compensation, but the dower (mahr) is not nullified because the father has no authority over her in this matter. If the khul' was for the dower, she can claim it from the husband, and the husband can claim it from the father due to his guarantee. If it was for something else, e.g., a thousand dirhams, she claims her dower from the husband, and the husband cannot claim it from the father because he only guaranteed the thousand, not the dower. Thus in al-Nahr.

He says: "If the payment is stipulated upon her" — meaning if the husband stipulates it upon the minor girl, he said in al-Hidaya: "If the thousand is stipulated upon her, it is suspended on her acceptance if she is capable of acceptance. If she accepts, divorce occurs due to the condition, and the payment is not obligatory because she is not subject to financial liability. If the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations."

End from al-Hidaya.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a father's khul' of his minor daughter. The text presents the soundest opinion (al-ashah) that the khul' is valid if the father guarantees the payment, and the divorce takes effect upon his acceptance. The alternative view argued that since the khul' is suspended on financial liability, and the minor is not liable, the divorce should not occur. However, the soundest opinion holds that the condition is the father's acceptance, which is valid. The father must pay the compensation, but the minor retains her right to dower from the husband. If the husband stipulates the payment on the minor, the divorce is suspended on her own acceptance if she is capable (i.e., she understands the consequences). If she accepts, divorce occurs but she owes nothing because she is not legally obligated. If the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations. The text clarifies that the father's role is as a guarantor (damin), not a surety (kafil), because there is no primary debtor here.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife or her guardian in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
ضامن (damin): One who undertakes to pay the compensation; differs from kafil (surety) as there is no primary debtor.
صغيرة (saghirah): A minor girl who has not reached puberty; her father has authority to act on her behalf in marriage and khul'.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The compensation paid by the wife or her guardian to the husband in exchange for divorce.
مهر (mahr): The dower payable by the husband to the wife; in this case, the father's guarantee does not affect the wife's right to her dower.
غرامة (gharamah): Financial liability; a minor is not subject to gharamah, so if the condition is on her, she owes nothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the soundest opinion, when does the divorce take effect in the father's khul' of his minor daughter?
A) When the father pays the compensation
B) When the father accepts the khul' on her behalf
C) When the minor girl herself accepts
D) When the husband receives the payment

Key Takeaway
The father's khul' of his minor daughter is valid if he guarantees the payment; the divorce occurs upon his acceptance, not the minor's liability.

Zihar: Definition and Quranic Basis
Defining zihar and providing its Quranic foundation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define zihar, state its legal effect, and identify the Quranic verses that form its basis.

Core Idea
Zihar is not divorce; it is a prohibition requiring expiation, rooted in the story of Khawlah and Aws.

This lesson opens the chapter on zihar (ظهار) by first explaining its placement after khul' and then defining the term. You will learn the linguistic and legal meaning of zihar, its Quranic foundation in Surah al-Mujadilah, and the occasion of revelation involving Khawlah bint Malik and Aws ibn Samit. The passage also clarifies that zihar applies only to wives, not to slave women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic origin
Zihar is derived from 'zahara' meaning to liken; it is a verbal noun with kasra on the za.
2
Understand the legal definition
The husband says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' implying she is like a mahram, making marital relations prohibited until expiation.
3
Connect to the Quranic basis
Surah al-Mujadilah (58:1-4) is cited as the primary evidence, including the story of Khawlah and Aws.
4
Note the exclusion of slave women
The text explicitly excludes slave women from zihar; it only applies to wives by legal definition.
5
Distinguish from khul'
Both zihar and khul' arise from nushuz, but khul' is more severe because it annuls marriage, hence placed before zihar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار

[١] قوله : باب الظهار؛ مناسبته بالخلع أن كلاً منهما يكون عن نشوز غالباً، والخلع لما كان أكمل في باب التحريم؛ لكونه رافعاً للنكاح قدمه على الظهار – وهو بكسر الظاء المعجمة - مصدر ظاهر من امرأته إذا قال لها: أنت علي كظهر أمي. والأصل في هذا الباب قوله تعالى في سورة المجادلة: ﴿قَدْ سَمِعَ اللَّهُ قَوْلَ الَّتِي تُجَادِلُكَ فِي زَوْجِهَا وَتَشْتَكِي إِلَى اللَّهِ وَاللَّهُ يَسْمَعُ تَحَاوُرَكُمَا إِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ بَصِيرٌ﴾ إلى قوله: ﴿فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَتَمَاسَّا﴾ الآيات. وكان نزول هذه الآيات حين ظاهر أوس بن صامت من زوجته خولة بنت مالك، وجاءت تشتكي إلى رسول الله ﷺ، كما أخرجه الحاكم وأبو داود وابن ماجه وغيرهم مفصلاً.

[٢] قوله : هو تشبيه زوجته؛ إضافة إلى المفعول، واحترز به عن أمته، فلا ظهار معها شرعاً كما سيأتي، والمراد بالتشبيه أعم من أن يكون صريحاً أو ضمناً، كما لو [ناقص]
Chapter of Zihar

[1] He says: “Chapter of Zihar” — its connection to khul' is that both usually arise from nushuz (disobedience). Since khul' is more complete in the chapter of prohibition because it annuls the marriage, it was placed before zihar. Zihar (with kasra of the dotted za) is the masdar (verbal noun) of ‘zahara’ from his wife, when he says to her: “You are to me like the back of my mother.” The basis of this chapter is the saying of Allah the Exalted in Surah al-Mujadilah: “Indeed Allah has heard the statement of her who pleads with you concerning her husband...” up to “...then the freeing of a slave before they touch each other.” These verses were revealed when Aws ibn Samit pronounced zihar against his wife Khawlah bint Malik, and she came complaining to the Messenger of Allah, as reported by Al-Hakim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and others in detail.

[2] He says: “It is the likening of his wife” — the addition is to the object (wife), and by this he excludes his female slave, so there is no zihar with her legally as will come. The meaning of likening is general, whether explicit or implicit, as if... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zihar (ظهار). The author first explains why the chapter on khul' precedes zihar: both are often related to marital discord (nushuz), but khul' is more severe in prohibition because it dissolves the marriage, whereas zihar only imposes a temporary prohibition requiring expiation. The term zihar is defined linguistically and legally: it comes from ‘zahara’ (to liken) and refers to a husband saying to his wife, “You are to me like the back of my mother.” This is an abhorrent and false statement, as Allah says in Surah al-Mujadilah. The Quranic verses from 1-4 are quoted as the primary source. The story of Khawlah bint Malik and Aws ibn Samit is mentioned as the occasion of revelation. The definition specifies that zihar applies only to wives, not slave women. The likening can be explicit (saying the words) or implicit (by implication). The text is cut off at “as if...” but the point is that the form of likening may vary.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband saying to his wife, 'You are like my mother's back,' which is a form of divorce-like prohibition requiring expiation.
تشبيه (tashbih): Likening; zihar is a tashbih of the wife to a mahram relative (mother).
نشوز (nushuz): Marital disobedience by the wife; both khul' and zihar often arise from nushuz.
أمة (ammah): Female slave; zihar is not valid with a slave woman because she is not like a wife's back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic basis for the ruling on zihar?
A) Surah al-Baqarah verse 230
B) Surah al-Mujadilah verses 1-4
C) Surah al-Nisa verse 34
D) Surah al-Talaq verse 1

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice prohibited in Islam; it does not divorce the wife but imposes a temporary prohibition requiring expiation, with its foundation in Surah al-Mujadilah.

The Impotent Man (al-ʻanīn) in Hanafi Law: Definition and Judicial Ruling
Definition and ruling with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-ʻanīn according to the Hanafi school, identify the categories included in its ruling, and state the judge's action when the man confesses inability.

Core Idea
An impotent man is one unable to consummate vaginally; the judge grants a one-year lunar respite for treatment.

This lesson explores the Hanafi definition of impotence (al-ʻanīn) and the related judicial ruling. The text defines the term broadly and includes related conditions such as al-majbūb, al-khaṣī, and al-shakkāz. The key ruling is that if the man confesses his inability to consummate, the judge gives him one lunar year to seek a cure. The passage also clarifies that the marriage is valid from the outset, even if the wife knows of the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
The passage is about the impotent man (al-ʻanīn). The ruling is: if he confesses he has not consummated, the judge gives him a respite of one lunar year.
The confession is a condition for the judge's action.
2
Understand the definition of al-ʻanīn
Al-ʻanīn is a man who cannot have vaginal intercourse despite having the organ. The definition covers various causes: illness, physical weakness, old age, magic, etc. It also includes cases where he can perform anal intercourse but not vaginal, or can reach some women but not others.
The key is the inability to penetrate vaginally.
3
Recognize related categories
The text mentions al-majbūb (penis and testicles removed), al-khaṣī (testicles only removed), and al-shakkāz (ejaculates before penetration). These are included in the same ruling as the ʻanīn.
These categories are treated similarly in terms of the judge's respite.
4
Grasp the rationale for one lunar year
The one-year period is specifically lunar because the Companions established it that way, and Islamic law uses lunar months. The year gives the man time to treat any illness or condition.
The text says 'in the correct view' (fī al-ṣaḥīḥ) to emphasize that the lunar year is the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العنين
إن أقر أنه لم يصل إليها أجله الحاكم سنة قمرية في الصحيح
[1] قوله : باب العنين ؛ لما فرغ عن أحكام النكاح والطلاق بأقسامه وما يتعلّق بها ، وكانت أحكام من به نوع مرض مغايرة من وجه لأحكام الأصحاء أفرد لها باباً على حدة، وذكر في العنوانِ العِنين فقط ؛ لأنه الأصل في الباب، والعِنّينُ - بكسر العين وتشديد النون الأولى المكسورة - وهو بمعنى مفعول، مأخوذ من عن بمعنى حبس، وقيل من عن عن الشيء بمعنى أعرض وهو من لا يقدر على جماع زوجته أو غيرها مع وجود الآلة، ولا فرق بين أن تنتشر أو لا تنتشر، وبين أن يصل إلى الثيب دون البكر، أو إلى بعض النساء دون بعض، فهو عِنين في حق من لا يصل إليه، وبين أن يكون ذلك لمرض به أو لضعف في خلقته أو كبر سنه، أو لسحر أو لغير ذلك، ولو قدر على الوطء في الدبر دون القبل فهو عنين. كذا في «العناية»(1) و«البحر»(2).
وفي حكمه : المجبوب : وهو مقطوع الذكر والانثيين.
والخصي ؛ أي مقطوع الانثيين فقط. والشكاز : وهو من إذا جَذَبَ بالمرأةِ أنزل قبل أن يخالطها، والنكاح بالعنين صحيح، وإن علمت بذلك حين النكاح، وكذا غيره، صرح به في «البحر» [2] قوله : أجله ؛ من التأجيل، أي أمهله القاضي سنة ؛ لاشتمالها على الفصول الأربعة، فيداوي ما كان به من مرض أو سحر أو نحو ذلك.
[3]قوله : في الصحيح ؛ وجهه : أنَّ الثابت في هذا الباب من الصحابة تأجيل سنة، وأهل الشرع إنّما كانوا يتعارفونَ الأشهر والسنين بالأهلة، فإذا أطلقوا السنة انصرف إلى ذلك ما لم يصرحوا بخلافه.

Chapter of the impotent man. If he confesses that he has not reached her, the judge gives him a period of one lunar year according to the correct [view]. [1] His statement: 'Chapter of the impotent man' – when he finished with the rulings of marriage and divorce and their divisions and what pertains to them, and since the rulings of one who has a type of illness are different in some respects from the rulings of the healthy, he dedicated a separate chapter to it. He mentioned only 'al-ʻanīn' in the title because it is the basis of the chapter. Al-ʻanīn – with kasra on the ʻayn and tashdeed on the first noon (maksūra) – it is in the sense of mafʻūl (passive), derived from ʻanna meaning 'to detain', and it is said [it is derived] from ʻanna ʻan al-shay' meaning 'to turn away'. He is one who is unable to have intercourse with his wife or others despite having the organ. There is no difference between whether [the organ] becomes erect or not, nor between whether he can reach a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others – he is ʻanīn with respect to the one he cannot reach – nor between whether that is due to an illness, a physical weakness, old age, magic, or other causes. If he is able to penetrate anally but not vaginally, he is ʻanīn. This is [as stated] in al-ʻInāya and al-Bahr. Included in the same ruling are: al-majbūb – one whose penis and testicles are cut off; al-khaṣī – one whose testicles only are cut off; and al-shakkāz – one who, upon drawing near to the woman, ejaculates before actual contact. Marriage with an impotent man is valid, even if the wife knew of this at the time of marriage, and likewise others – this is explicitly stated in al-Bahr. [2] His statement: 'ajalahu' (gives him a period) – from taʼjīl (postponement), meaning the judge gives him a respite of one year because it includes the four seasons, during which he can treat whatever illness, magic, or similar he has. [3] His statement: 'fī al-ṣaḥīḥ' (in the correct view) – its reasoning: what is established in this chapter from the Companions is the postponement of one year, and the people of Islamic law (ahl al-sharʻ) would only recognize months and years by the lunar months. Thus, when they absolutely mention 'year', it refers to [the lunar year] unless they explicitly state otherwise.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the impotent man (al-ʻanīn) in a Hanafi fiqh text. The author first defines the term 'al-ʻanīn' linguistically as derived from 'ʻanna' meaning 'to detain' or 'to turn away', and technically as a man who is unable to have vaginal intercourse with his wife despite having a functioning organ. The definition is broad: it covers inability due to illness, weakness, old age, magic, etc., and includes cases where he can only perform anal intercourse. The author then mentions three related categories: al-majbūb (penis and testes removed), al-khaṣī (testes only removed), and al-shakkāz (premature ejaculation before penetration). The ruling from the matn is that if the man confesses his inability, the judge gives him a respite of one lunar year. The commentary explains that 'year' here means a lunar year, based on the practice of the Companions, because Islamic legal usage of months and years is by the lunar calendar. The judge grants this year so the man can seek treatment. The marriage of an impotent man is valid from the outset, even if the wife knows of his condition. This passage is a typical Hanafi presentation of a ruling with definition and justification.

Key Terms
العنين (al-ʻanīn): A man who cannot have vaginal intercourse with his wife due to organ failure, illness, or other causes, with the organ existing.
المجبوب (al-majbūb): A man whose penis and testicles are both cut off.
الخصي (al-khaṣī): A man whose testicles are cut off but penis remains.
الشكاز (al-shakkāz): A man who ejaculates before penetration during intercourse.

Nikah — Marriage

The 'Innin: Definition, Ruling, and the One-Year Delay
Defines 'innin and rules on the one-year delay for consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of al-‘innin, identify the related conditions (majbub, khasi, shakkaz), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the judge’s one-year delay is a lunar or solar year, citing the evidence for each view and the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The 'innin is anyone who cannot consummate vaginally; the judge grants a one-year delay – lunar year is the relied view, solar year is a cautionary minority view.

This passage from ‘Umdat al-Ri‘aya on Sharh al-Wiqaya introduces the chapter on the impotent man (al-‘innin). It defines the term broadly, including cases where the husband can only achieve anal intercourse, and clarifies that the marriage remains valid. The central legal question is the duration of the judge’s delay: one year, but is it a lunar year of 354 days or a solar year of 365 days? This lesson unpacks the definition and the internal Hanafi debate on the calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and conditions
What is the Hanafi definition of ‘innin? What conditions are included and excluded? Note the related terms: majbub, khasi, shakkaz.
2
State the basic rulings
The marriage of an ‘innin is valid. Upon his admission, the judge gives a one-year delay for treatment.
3
Locate the evidence
The Companions’ practice (qawl sahabi) of giving a one-year deferment is the primary proof.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
What is the Zahir al-Riwayah position? (lunar year). What is the narration from Hasan? (solar year). What are the arguments for each?
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical difference
Which view is relied upon and why? How does it affect the wife’s right to seek annulment after the delay?

Chapter of the impotent man: If he admits that he did not reach her (consummate), the judge gives him a lunar year according to the correct view. His statement: Chapter of the impotent man; when he finished with the rulings of marriage and divorce and their sections and what pertains to them, and since the rulings of one who has a type of illness are different in some respect from the rulings of the healthy, he dedicated a separate chapter for it. In the title he mentioned only 'al-'innin' because it is the basis of the chapter. Al-'innin (with kasra on the 'ayn and tashdid on the first nun which is also kasra) is in the sense of maf'ul, derived from 'anna meaning to restrain, or it is said from 'anna 'an al-shay' meaning to turn away. It is one who cannot have intercourse with his wife or others despite the presence of the organ, and there is no difference between whether it becomes erect or not, between whether he can penetrate a previously married woman but not a virgin, or some women but not others; he is 'innin in respect to the one he cannot reach, and whether that is due to an illness, a congenital weakness, old age, sorcery, or otherwise. If he is able to have anal intercourse but not vaginal, he is 'innin. Thus in al-'Inaya and al-Bahr. Included in its ruling: al-majbub: one whose penis and testicles are cut off. Al-khasi: one whose testicles only are cut off. Al-shakkaz: one who when he draws near the woman ejaculates before penetrating. The marriage of the 'innin is valid, even if she knew that at the time of marriage, and likewise others, as stated in al-Bahr. His statement: ajal (time limit); from ta'jil, meaning the judge gives him a delay of one year because it includes the four seasons, so he can treat whatever illness, sorcery, or similar he has. His statement: 'in the correct view'; its reasoning: what is established in this chapter from the Companions is the deferral of one year, and the people of the Shari'a were accustomed to knowing months and years by the moons (lunar months), so when they use the term 'year' absolutely, it refers to that unless they explicitly state otherwise. (Footnote references). The narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa is that he gives him a solar year, but in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah): a lunar year. So the solar year is the duration of the sun's reaching the point it departed from in the zodiac, which is 365 and a quarter days. The lunar year is twelve lunar months, and its duration is 354 days, and one third of a day, and one third of a tenth of a day. This is the narration of the solar year, and a group of mashayikh chose it, like Qadi Khan and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi and others: that consideration is for the number of days, and in considering it there is a type of caution. Thus in al-Fath and others. And the reasoning. His statement: 'the solar year...' Know that it is established in its place that the sun and moon each move in their sphere by the permission of their Lord. The sun completes its cycle in a year, the moon in a month. Completion of the cycle means the arrival of the celestial body at the point from which it departed. Consideration in this chapter is for the zodiac, which is a sphere divided into twelve equal sections from pole to pole, called buruj (signs), each one is buruj (with damm). The great circle in its middle from east to west is called the zodiac belt. The sun cuts through each sign in approximately a month. In summary: the complete cycle of the sun occurs in 365 and a quarter days. The lunar year is twelve lunar months, and its duration is less than the solar year by about ten days. Details of these discussions are in the science of astronomy. His statement: 'and one third of a tenth of a day'; meaning a part of thirty parts of a day, and by 'day' here is meant the day with its night, its measure is forty hours. The commentator al-Harawi said in his commentary: The solar year is the time of the sun's departure from a certain assumed point of the zodiac by its own motion from west to east until its return to that point, and they consider that point as the beginning of Aries.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on al-Wiqayah, discussing the chapter on the impotent man (al-'innin). It begins by defining the term: a man who cannot have vaginal intercourse with his wife or any woman despite having a male organ, whether due to erectile issues, physical weakness, old age, sorcery, etc. Importantly, if he can only perform anal intercourse, he is still considered 'innin. The text then clarifies that the rulings also apply to similar conditions: al-majbub (castrated), al-khasi (whose testicles are removed), and al-shakkaz (who ejaculates prematurely). A key ruling is that the marriage of an 'innin is valid, even if the wife knew of his condition at the time of the contract. The core legal discussion concerns the judge's procedure: if the husband admits he has not consummated the marriage, the judge grants him a one-year delay. This is based on the practice of the Companions. The delay is meant to allow for treatment of any underlying condition. A significant intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding whether the year is solar or lunar. The Zahir al-Riwayah (the established transmission) says it is a lunar year, based on the common usage of the term 'year' in Shari'a referring to lunar months. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa states it is a solar year, which is longer (365.25 days vs. 354 days). A number of later scholars, such as Qadi Khan and al-Sarakhsi, chose the solar year on the basis of caution (ihtiyat) and numerical days. The passage then provides an astronomical explanation of both solar and lunar years, referencing the zodiac and celestial motions, concluding that the details belong to the science of astronomy (hay'a). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the text is the lunar year from Zahir al-Riwayah, but the solar year is also considered a valid opinion chosen by some major scholars.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'innin): A man who cannot have vaginal intercourse with his wife or any woman despite possessing a male organ, due to any cause (illness, weakness, old age, sorcery, etc.).
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis and testicles are both cut off, making him completely incapable of intercourse.
الخصي (al-khasi): A man whose testicles are removed but penis remains; considered in the same ruling as 'innin if he cannot penetrate.
الشكاز (al-shakkaz): A man who ejaculates immediately upon approaching his wife before penetration.
السنة القمرية (al-sanat al-qamariyya): The lunar year of 12 lunar months, approximately 354 days, used in Islamic calendar.
السنة الشمسية (al-sanat al-shamsiyya): The solar year of approximately 365.25 days, based on the sun's motion through the zodiac.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One lunar year

Key Takeaway
The ‘innin’s marriage is valid; the judge grants a one-year delay (lunar year in the relied-upon view) for treatment, after which the wife may seek annulment.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on the Impotent Husband ('Iinin) and Deferment
Expounds on the deferment and separation process for an impotent husband with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the deferment and separation for an impotent husband, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the need for a judge, and explain why the separation is considered a bain divorce rather than faskh.

Core Idea
An impotent husband is given one year; if no intercourse, the wife may obtain a bain divorce — either by judge or her own choice.

The case of an impotent husband raises questions about the rights of the wife and the nature of marital obligations. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the husband is deferred for one year, after which the wife may seek separation. We will also explore the internal Hanafi disagreement on whether a judge is required and the dispute with the Shafi'i school on whether the separation is a divorce or annulment.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the husband is given one year to consummate; if he fails, the wife may seek separation, which is a bain (irrevocable) divorce.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Shafi'i holds that the separation is faskh (annulment), not divorce, because it originates from the wife's right.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i analogizes to khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) and khiyar al-itq (option of emancipation) where the wife can annul.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafi argues that after completion (valid seclusion), marriage cannot be annulled; the judge acts on the husband's behalf, making it a divorce.
Also note the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa requires judge; Sahibayn say wife can choose herself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if talaq bain, it counts as a divorce affecting the number of divorces; if faskh, no count. Also affects mahr and 'iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيام حيضها منها، لا مدة مرضه ومرضها (۱)، فإن لم يصل فيها فرق القاضي بينهما إن طلبته (۲): أي إن طلبت المرأة التفريق معه. ولا تحتسب مدة حجها وغيبتها؛ لأن العجز من قبلها، فكان عذراً، فيعوض، وكذا لو حبس الزوج ولو بمهرها وامتنعت من المجيء إلى السجن، فإن لم تمتنع وكان له موضع خلوة فيه احتسب عليه. وأما مدة مرضهما فلا تحتسب من مدة التأجيل، بل تعوض عنها أيام أخر؛ لأن السنة قد تخلو عنه، وليس هو باختياري لأحدهما، والمراد به المرض الذي لا يستطيع الوطء. كذا في «العناية» و«الفتح» وغيرهما.
[١] قوله: فإن لم يصل؛ أي إن لم يطأها الزوج في السنة ولو مرة، فإن وطئها مرة أيضاً كفى ذلك دافعاً لدعواها.
[٢] قوله: فرق؛ ماض من التفريق، ونسبته إلى القاضي تشير إلى أنه لا تقع الفرقة بنفس مضي السنة، بل ينظر بعده إن طلقها فيها، وإن أبى طلاقها ناب عنه القاضي؛ لأنه وجب على الزوج التسريح بالإحسان حين عجز عن الإمساك بالمعروف، فإذا امتنع كان ظالماً، فناب عنه. وقيل: لا حاجة إلى القاضي، بل يكفي اختيارها نفسها، كخيار العتق، ونسب صاحب «مجمع البحرين» الأول إلى الإمام، والثاني إليهما، وحكم في «غاية البيان» على الثاني بأنه الأصح.
[٣] قوله: إن طلبته؛ إنما قيد به؛ لأن ذلك حق المرأة، فلا بد من طلبها، وهذا الطلب طلب للتفريق، والأول كان طلباً للتأجيل، والأصل في هذا الباب ما روي عن عمر: أنه قضى في العنين أن يؤجل سنة (۳)، أخرجه عبد الرزاق والدارقطني ومحمد بن الحسن في كتاب «الآثار».
(۳) فعن عمر أنه قال في العنين: يؤجل سنة، فإن وصل إليها، وإلا فرق بينهما ولها المهر كاملا، وهي تطليقة بائنة. أخرجه في «الآثار» لأبي يوسف (۲: ۱۵۲)، و«السنن الصغير» (۵: ۳۹۶)، و«سنن الدارقطني» (۳: ۲۶۷)، و«مصنف عبد الرزاق» (۶: ۲۵۳)، وغيرها.
ثم قال الماتن: وتبين بطلقة، ولها كل المهر إن خلا بها، وتجب العدة، وإن اختلفا.
وتبين بطلقة، ولها كل المهر إن خلا بها، وتجب العدة. التأجيل.
وإن اختلفا: عطف على قوله: إن أقر، فالمراد الاختلاف ابتداءً لا بعد.
وفي رواية: «فلما مضى الأجل خيرها فاختارت نفسها، ففرق بينهما»، ونحوه أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة عنه، وعبد الرزاق عن علي (۱)، وابن أبي شيبة وعبد الرزاق والدارقطني عن ابن مسعود (۲).
[١] قوله: وتبين؛ أي تصير الزوجة بائنة، فيكون هذا التفريق طلاقاً بائناً. وعند الشافعي: هذا التفريق فسخ؛ لكونه فرقة من جهتها، كما في خيار البلوغ، وخيار العتق. ونحن نقول: النكاح لا يقبل الفسخ بعد التمام، وأما قبل التمام فيقبله، كما في الخيارين المذكورين، فإنه امتناع عن تمام العقد، ولما كان الواجب على الزوج التسريح بالإحسان وناب القاضي عنه دفعاً للظلم عنها، صار فعله مضافاً إليه، فكأنه طلقها بنفسه، وإنما كان الطلاق بائناً؛ لأن المقصود هو التسريح، ودفع الظلم يحصل فيه، فإن الرجعي تحل فيه الرجعة.
[٢] قوله: ولها؛ أي يجب عليه كل المهر إن وقعت الخلوة بينهما، فإن خلوة العنين صحيحة؛ لسلامة الآلة.
[٣] قوله: وتجب العدة؛ أي بعد التفريق الذي هو في حكم الطلاق البائن، وجوبها احتياطي؛ لتوهم شغل الرحم.
[٤] قوله: وإن اختلفا... الخ؛ حاصله: إنه إذا خاصمته المرأة فإن أقر أنه لم يطأها أجل سنة بطلبها على التفصيل الذي مر، وإن أنكر وادعى وطأها ولو مرة، أمر القاضي النساء العارفات ينظرن هل هي الآن ثيب أو بكر، فإن قلن: ثيب، فالقول له بيمينه، وإن قلن: بكر، أجل، وكذا إن نكل.
(۱) في «مصنف ابن أبي شيبة» (۳: ۵۰۳)، و«سنن البيهقي الكبير» (۷: ۲۲۶)، وغيرها.
(۲) ينظر: «الدراية» (ص ۷۶).
And [counted] are the days of her menses from it, not the period of his illness and her illness. If he did not have intercourse in it, the judge separates them if she requests it, meaning if the woman requests separation from him. And the period of her Hajj and her absence is not counted because the inability is from her side, so it is an excuse, so it is compensated. Similarly, if the husband is imprisoned even for her mahr and she refrains from coming to the prison, but if she does not refrain and he has a place of seclusion there, it is counted against him. As for the period of their illness, it is not counted from the period of deferment, rather other days are compensated for it, because the year may be free of it, and it is not voluntary for either of them. What is meant is the illness in which intercourse is not possible. Thus in al-'Inayah and al-Fath and others. [1] His saying: 'If he did not have intercourse' means if the husband did not have intercourse with her in the year at least once, for if he had intercourse with her once, that suffices to repel her claim. [2] His saying: 'separates' is past tense from tafriq, and its attribution to the judge indicates that the separation does not occur by the mere passing of the year, rather he looks after it: if he divorced her in it, but if he refuses to divorce her, the judge acts on his behalf, because the husband is obligated to release with kindness when he is unable to retain her with honor, and if he refuses, he is a wrongdoer, so the judge acts on his behalf. And it is said: there is no need for the judge, rather her own choice suffices, like the option of emancipation. The author of Majma' al-Bahrain attributes the first to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the second to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and ruled in Ghayat al-Bayan that the second is the most correct. [3] His saying: 'if she requests it' is restricted because that is the right of the woman, so her request is necessary. This request is a request for separation, while the first was a request for deferment. The origin in this chapter is what is narrated from 'Umar: that he ruled regarding the impotent man that he should be deferred for a year, as recorded by 'Abd al-Razzaq, al-Daraqutni, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in the book al-Athar. (3) From 'Umar: he said about the impotent man: 'He is deferred for a year; if he reaches her, else separate them, and she gets the full mahr, and it is a bain divorce.' Recorded in al-Athar of Abu Yusuf (2:152), al-Sunan al-Saghir (5:396), Sunan al-Daraqutni (3:267), Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq (6:253), etc. Then the author said: 'And she becomes separated with one pronouncement, and she gets the full mahr if he had seclusion with her, and 'iddah is obligatory, and if they differ.' 'And she becomes separated with one pronouncement, and she gets the full mahr if he had seclusion with her, and 'iddah is obligatory. The deferment.' 'And if they differ' is conjunctive to his saying 'if he acknowledges', meaning the difference initially, not afterward. In a narration: 'When the period passed, he gave her choice, so she chose her own self, and he separated between them.' Something similar was recorded by Ibn Abi Shaybah from him, and 'Abd al-Razzaq from 'Ali (1), and Ibn Abi Shaybah, 'Abd al-Razzaq, and al-Daraqutni from Ibn Mas'ud (2). [1] His saying: 'And she becomes separated' means the wife becomes bainah, so this separation is a bain divorce. According to al-Shafi'i: this separation is a faskh (annulment), because it is a separation from her side, as in the option of puberty and the option of emancipation. We say: marriage does not accept faskh after completion, but before completion it accepts it, as in the two mentioned options, for it is a refusal to complete the contract. Since the husband is obligated to release with kindness and the judge acts on his behalf to remove injustice from her, his action becomes attributed to him, as if he divorced her himself. It is a bain divorce because the purpose is release, and removal of injustice is achieved in it, for in revocable divorce, return (raj'ah) is permissible. [2] His saying: 'And she gets' means he must pay the full mahr if seclusion occurred between them, because the seclusion of the impotent man is valid due to the soundness of the organ. [3] His saying: 'And 'iddah is obligatory' means after the separation which is like a bain divorce, its obligation is precautionary due to the possibility of the womb being occupied. [4] His saying: 'And if they differ...' etc.; the summary: if the woman litigates with him, and he acknowledges that he did not have intercourse, she is deferred for a year by her request in the detail that has passed. If he denies and claims intercourse even once, the judge orders knowledgeable women to see whether she is now a thayyib or a virgin. If they say: thayyib, then his word with his oath is taken; if they say: virgin, he is deferred; similarly if he declines to swear. (1) In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (3:503), and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (7:226), etc. (2) See: al-Dirayah (p. 76).
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rulings regarding an impotent husband ('innin) from al-Hidayah and al-Wiqayah. The commentary clarifies that the one-year deferment period does not count days of the wife's menses or periods of illness for either spouse that prevent intercourse, since these are not voluntary. However, if the wife is away for Hajj or imprisoned, those days are not counted against the husband because the inability is from her side. If the husband is imprisoned and the wife refuses to visit, similarly the days are not counted unless she comes and there is a place for seclusion.

A key point: the separation does not occur automatically after a year; the wife must request it, and the judge must act if the husband refuses to divorce her. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the judge's intervention is necessary, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the wife's own choice suffices, like the option of emancipation. The commentator in Ghayat al-Bayan rules the second view as more correct.

The proof is the ruling of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) which is the basis for this chapter. The text then addresses the consequences: the separation is a bain (irrevocable) divorce, not an annulment as al-Shafi'i holds. The Hanafi reasoning: after the marriage is complete (with consummation or valid seclusion), it cannot be annulled; thus the separation is a divorce. Since it is bain, the wife gets full mahr if seclusion occurred (since seclusion by an impotent man is valid as his organ is sound). 'Iddah is obligatory precautionary.

Finally, if the husband claims he did have intercourse, the judge appoints women to examine the wife to determine if she is still a virgin or not. If they find her a thayyib (non-virgin), the husband's claim is accepted with his oath; if they find her a virgin, he is deferred.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'innin): A man who cannot have intercourse due to a physical defect, whether congenital or acquired.
التأجيل (al-ta'jil): The one-year deferment granted to the impotent husband to attempt intercourse before separation.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-bain): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what kind of separation occurs when a judge separates an impotent husband from his wife after a one-year deferment?
A) Revocable divorce (talaq raj'i)
B) Irrevocable divorce (talaq bain)
C) Annulment (faskh) like khiyar al-bulugh
D) No divorce; the marriage remains

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the wife of an impotent husband may obtain a bain divorce after a one-year deferment, either by judge's decree or by her own choice, distinguishing it from annulment.

Khiyar al-'Ayb: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Annulment for Defects
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on option due to defects in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khiyar al-'ayb, explain the Shafi'i counter-position, and identify the practical difference between the two schools.

Core Idea
Hanafi: no general right to annul for defects; only the woman can annul for severe impairments.

Marriage is a strong contract, but what if one spouse has a serious defect? The schools differ sharply. This passage presents the Hanafi view that neither spouse can annul the marriage due to defects, except the woman in extreme cases, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view giving the husband broader options. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on the contract's permanence and the limited grounds for dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The dispute is about khiyar al-faskh (right to annul) due to defects in the other spouse. The Hanafi school holds that neither spouse generally has this right, while al-Shafi'i holds that the husband has it for five specified defects.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, no option exists for either spouse. The default principle is the absence of option; exceptions are only for the wife in cases of impotence, insanity, leprosy, and vitiligo because these impair the essential purpose (intercourse) or cause direct harm.
The Hanafi position is attributed to 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Al-Shafi'i gives the husband an option to annul if the wife has one of five defects: ratq, qarn, leprosy, and others. The reasoning is that these defects prevent full enjoyment, either physically or by natural repulsion.
The five defects include physical obstructions and contagious diseases.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that these defects do not impair the fundamental purpose of marriage (intercourse) as impotence does. Any repulsion can be resolved through divorce (talaq) or khul', not annulment. Thus, analogy to impotence fails.
The text cites 'al-Fath' and 'al-Nihaya' as sources for the rebuttal.
5
Determine the practical difference
In practice, a Hanafi husband cannot annul the marriage if his wife has any defect; he can only divorce her. A Shafi'i husband can annul if the wife has one of the five defects. The Hanafi wife has a limited right to annul for severe defects, while under Shafi'i law she must rely on the husband's option.
This thamarah al-khilaf affects the legal remedy available to each spouse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتخير أحدهما بعيب الآخر، خلافاً للشافعي له في العيوب الخمسة. [1] قوله: ولا يتخير؛ أي ليس لواحدٍ منهما خيار فسخ النكاح بعيب في الآخر عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وهو قول علي وابن مسعود. وعند الشافعي: إذا كان بالزوجة أحد العيوب الخمسة فله الخيار؛ لأنها تمنع تمام الاستيفاء حساً كما في الرتق والقرن، أو طبعاً كما في الجذام وغيره، فإن الطبع يتنفر من جماع هؤلاء. وقال محمد: لا خيار له في عيوبها، ولها الخيار إذا كان مجنوناً أو مبروصاً أو مجذوماً دفعاً للضرر عنها كما في الحب والعنة. ولهما: إن الأصل هو عدم الخيار، وإنما يثبت لها في العنّة ونحوها؛ لأنه يخلّ بأصل المقصود، وهو الوطء، وهذه العيوب غير مخلة بأصل المقصود، فلا تكون في معنى العنّة حتى تقاس عليها، والتنفّر الطبعي أو العجز الحسي عن تمام الاستيفاء يمكن دفعه بطلاقها من جانبه، أو بالخلع ونحوه من جانبها كذا في «الفتح» و«النهاية».
And neither of them has the option due to a defect in the other, contrary to al-Shafi'i who gives it for the five defects. [1] His statement: and neither has the option; meaning that neither has the option to annul the marriage due to a defect in the other according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is the saying of 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. According to al-Shafi'i: if the wife has one of the five defects, the husband has the option because they prevent complete enjoyment, either physically as in ratq and qarn, or by nature as in leprosy and others, for nature is repulsed by intercourse with such persons. Muhammad said: he has no option for her defects, but she has the option if he is insane, has leprosy, or has vitiligo, to ward off harm from her, as in the case of 'inn and 'ina. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: The principle is that there is no option, and it is established for her only in 'inna and the like because it impairs the original purpose, which is intercourse. These defects do not impair the original purpose, so they are not like 'inna to be analogized to it. Natural repulsion or physical inability to complete enjoyment can be avoided by his divorcing her or by her seeking khul'. So in 'al-Fath' and 'al-Nihaya'.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about whether spouses have the right to annul the marriage due to defects (khiyar al-'ayb). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that neither spouse has such an option. This is based on the principle that the marriage contract is not invalidated by defects; the only relief is through divorce or khul'. However, the woman is given the option specifically in cases of impotence, insanity, leprosy, and vitiligo because these impair the essential purpose (intercourse) or cause direct harm. Al-Shafi'i holds that the husband has the option if the wife has one of five specified defects (ratq, qarn, leprosy, etc.) because they prevent full enjoyment. The Hanafi response argues that these defects do not fundamentally impair the purpose of marriage as impotence does, and any repulsion can be resolved by divorce or khul' rather than annulment. The passage concludes by citing 'al-Fath' and 'al-Nihaya' as sources.

Key Terms
خيار الفسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Right to annul the marriage contract due to a defect
رتق (ratq): A condition in which the woman's vagina is closed or blocked
قرن (qarn): A growth or obstruction in the vagina
جذام (judham): Leprosy
برص (baras): Vitiligo or leprosy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a husband discovers his wife has a condition (like ratq) that makes intercourse difficult, does he have the right to annul the marriage?
A) Yes, because it prevents full enjoyment.
B) No, he does not have that option; he can divorce her.
C) Yes, but only if he did not know before marriage.
D) No, only the wife has options for defects.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school denies a general right to annul for defects; the wife's option is limited to severe impairments that destroy the essential purpose of marriage.

Delay for the Eunuch and Immediate Separation for the Amputee
Ruling on delay for khasi and immediate separation for majbub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ruling for a eunuch (khasi) and an amputee (majbub) regarding delay before annulment, and state the reason based on the possibility of intercourse.

Core Idea
A eunuch is given a delay because intercourse is expected; an amputee is separated immediately because it is impossible.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school differentiates between two types of male reproductive defects in marriage: the eunuch (khasi), whose testicles are removed, and the one whose penis is amputated (majbub). The school rules that the wife may annul the marriage immediately for the majbub, but must wait a year for the eunuch, analogizing him to an impotent man. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing the illa (ratio legis): the presence or absence of the organ of intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage defines 'khasi' as a man whose testicles are removed but his penis remains, and 'majbub' as a man whose penis is amputated (along with testicles). Recognize that the legal rule depends on these definitions.
Khasi is on the pattern fa'il; majbub is the one whose penis is cut off.
2
State the ruling for each
The eunuch is treated like an impotent man regarding delay: the wife must wait one year before seeking annulment. The majbub is separated from the wife immediately upon her request.
The delay for the impotent man is a year in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the illa (reason)
Delay is prescribed so that the husband may undergo treatment to become capable of intercourse. This is possible for the eunuch because he still has the organ, but impossible for the majbub because the organ is absent. Thus, no benefit in delaying for the majbub.
The illa is the possibility of achieving the primary objective of marriage: intercourse.
4
Note the wife's role
The separation for the majbub occurs 'at her request', indicating that the option belongs to the wife. She can choose to annul immediately or remain married.
The option is not automatic; the wife must initiate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( ولا يتخير" أحدهما بعيب الآخر)، خلافاً للشافعي له في العيوب الخمسة [١] قوله : والخصي ؛ على وزن فعيل ، هو من تنزع خصيتاه، ويبقى ذكره، فإن قطعنا مع ذكره فهو المحبوب. [٢] قوله : إذ لا فائدة ؛ فإنّ التأجيل إنّما هو لأن يشتغل في العلاج وغيره من التدابير؛ ليصير قادراً على الوطء، وهذا مفقود في المجبوب ؛ لفقدان آلة الوطء فيه ، بخلاف الخصي ، فإنّ الذكر فيه موجود، فالوطئ منه مرجو. The eunuch is like the impotent man regarding delay, and regarding the one whose penis is amputated, separation occurs immediately, at her request. Neither of them has option due to the other's defect. (The eunuch is like the impotent man): meaning regarding delay. (Regarding the one whose penis is amputated, separation occurs immediately): meaning at that moment, (at her request): because there is no benefit in delaying him, unlike the eunuch, for intercourse is expected from him. (Neither of them has option due to the other's defect), contrary to al-Shafi'i, who allows it for the five defects. [1] The eunuch (al-khasi) is on the pattern of fa'il, he whose testicles are removed and his penis remains; if we cut it off along with his penis, then he is al-majbub. [2] There is no benefit: because delay is only so that he may engage in treatment and other measures to become able to have intercourse, and this is lacking in the one whose penis is amputated due to the absence of the organ of intercourse, unlike the eunuch, for the penis exists, so intercourse is hoped for from him. [3] Neither has option: meaning neither of them has the option to annul the marriage due to a defect in the other according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is the saying of Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. According to al-Shafi'i: if the wife has one of the five defects, he has the option because they prevent complete enjoyment physically, as in retq and qarn, or naturally as in leprosy and others, for nature abhors intercourse with such persons. Muhammad said: He has no option due to her defects, and she has the option if he is mad, vitiliginous, or leprous to ward off harm from herself, as in the case of the one imprisoned and the impotent. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The principle is the absence of option; it is only established for her in the case of impotence and the like, because it affects the primary objective, which is intercourse. These defects do not affect the primary objective, so they are not analogous to impotence to be measured against it. Natural aversion or physical inability to complete enjoyment can be avoided by his divorcing her, or by her seeking khul', etc. Thus in al-Fath and al-Nihayah. (2) (1) See: al-Umm (8): (277), al-Ghurar al-Bahiyya (4): (161), al-Mahalli 'ala al-Minhaj (3: 262), etc. (2) Fath al-Qadir (4: 304). The Book of Divorce, Chapter on the Impotent Man. They are: madness, leprosy, vitiligo, qarn, and retq. According to Muhammad: if the husband has madness, leprosy, or vitiligo, the wife has the option; if the wife has them, no, because the husband can ward off harm from himself by divorce. (1) Madness: loss of intellect. Leprosy: a bad disease arising from the spread of black bile. Vitiligo: whiteness appearing on the body, sometimes on some limbs, caused by poor temperament and excess phlegm and coldness. Qarn: an obstacle preventing the entry of the male organ into the vulva, such as bone etc. Retq: that she has no opening other than the urethra. Thus in al-Binaya. (3).
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the option of annulment (khiyar al-ayb) due to defects in marriage. The passage begins by distinguishing between the eunuch (khasi) and the one whose penis is amputated (majbub). The eunuch is given a delay like an impotent man, while the majbub is separated immediately at the wife's request because no benefit is expected. The author then states that neither spouse has the option to annul due to a defect in the other. This is the Hanafi position according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and it is attributed to Ali and Ibn Mas'ud. Al-Shafi'i holds that if the wife has one of five defects (madness, leprosy, vitiligo, qarn, retq), the husband has the option because these defects prevent complete enjoyment. The Hanafi response, attributed to Muhammad (possibly al-Shaybani) and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), argues that the option is only given to the wife in cases of impotence ('innah) because it hinders the primary objective of intercourse. Other defects, even if they cause aversion or partial difficulty, do not nullify the essential objective and can be addressed by divorce or khul'. Thus, the Hanafi school restricts the option of annulment for defects to specific cases like impotence, lunacy, leprosy, and vitiligo for the wife only. The passage ends by listing the five defects and clarifying that according to Muhammad, if the husband has certain defects the wife has the option, but not vice versa, because the husband can divorce. This commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling on delay, then the dispute on khiyar, and finally the enumeration of defects.

Key Terms
الخصي (al-khasi): A man whose testicles are removed but his penis remains; like an impotent man regarding delay.
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis is amputated (along with testicles); separation is immediate at wife's request.
العنن (al-'innah): Impotence; inability to have intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a woman married to a majbub?
A) She must wait one year before annulment.
B) She can annul the marriage immediately at her request.
C) She has no right to annul at all.
D) The marriage is automatically invalid.

Key Takeaway
The presence or absence of the male organ determines whether a delay is required before annulment: the eunuch must wait, the amputee is separated immediately.

Nikah — Marriage

The Option of Annulment Due to Defects: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on khiyar al-ayb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on khiyar al-ayb (option to annul due to defects) and contrast it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the five defects and the rationale for the difference.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, only severe defects that prevent intercourse give the wife the option to annul; the Shafi'i school gives the husband the option for five specific defects in the wife.

This lesson delves into the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the option to annul a marriage due to defects (khiyar al-ayb). The Hanafi school, as represented by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, restricts the option to the wife for defects that directly impede intercourse, such as impotence, madness, leprosy, and vitiligo in the husband. The Shafi'i school, conversely, grants the husband the option if the wife has any of five defects: madness, leprosy, vitiligo, qarn (a bony obstruction), or retq (vaginal atresia). The divergence stems from different assessments of which defects affect the essential purpose of marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The passage states that neither spouse has the option due to the other's defect according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. However, a variant (from Muhammad alone and from the two) gives the wife option if the husband is mad, leprous, or vitiliginous, in addition to impotence.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) adopts the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the wife has option for these three defects.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that if the wife has any of the five defects, the husband has the option to annul, because they prevent complete enjoyment physically (qarn, retq) or naturally (madness, leprosy, vitiligo).
The five defects are: جنون (madness), جذام (leprosy), برص (vitiligo), قرن (qarn), and رتق (retq).
3
Analyze the Hanafi rationale
The Hanafi response argues that the default is no option (الأصل عدم الخيار). The option is only established for the wife in cases like impotence because it directly undermines the primary objective of marriage (intercourse). Other defects do not affect this primary objective; they cause natural aversion or partial difficulty, which can be remedied by divorce or khul'.
The Hanafi school uses a strict analogy (qiyas) and does not extend the rule beyond the clear cases.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a Hanafi court, a husband cannot annul the marriage because his wife has any of the five defects. In a Shafi'i court, he can. Conversely, a wife in a Hanafi court can annul if her husband has impotence, madness, leprosy, or vitiligo; in a Shafi'i court, she cannot for these defects (but may for impotence under different rules).
This difference significantly affects the outcome of marriage annulment cases.

Source Text

Wife's Option for Husband's Defects in Marriage
Ruling on wife's option due to husband's defects with definitions and intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which defects in the husband give the wife the option to annul the marriage according to the Hanafi school, and identify Imam Muhammad's differing view.

Core Idea
The wife can annul the marriage if the husband has one of five specific defects; but Imam Muhammad restricts this to three.

In Hanafi marriage law, a wife may have the option to annul the contract if the husband suffers from certain defects. This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah lists five such defects and also presents a differing view from Imam Muhammad. In this lesson, we will unpack the defects and understand the scope of the wife's khiyar.

Guided Path
1
List the five defects
Identify the five defects mentioned: madness (junun), leprosy (judham), vitiligo (baras), bone growth (qarn), and closure (ratq).
2
Understand the general Hanafi rule
The general position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that the wife has an option to annul if any of these five defects exists in the husband.
3
Identify Imam Muhammad's restriction
Imam Muhammad limits the option to only three defects (madness, leprosy, vitiligo) and only when they are in the husband, not the wife.
His reasoning: the husband can divorce to remove harm from himself.
4
Comprehend the definitions
Study the lexical and medical definitions given for each defect to distinguish them clearly.
E.g., qarn is a bone growth obstructing intercourse; ratq is closure except for the urinary meatus.
5
Apply to scenarios
Given a specific defect, determine whether the wife has an option under each position.
Practice with different defects to see the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses the wife's option (khiyar) due to defects in marriage. The author lists five defects: madness (junūn), leprosy (judhām), vitiligo (baraṣ), a bone growth (qarn), and closure (ratq). The main ruling is that if any of these defects exist in the husband, the wife has the option to annul the marriage. Then the author mentions the view of Imam Muhammad: according to him, this option applies only when the defects exist in the husband; if they are in the wife, she has no option, because the husband can easily divorce her to remove harm. The commentary then defines each term lexically and medically, explaining the causes. This is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: the general position (of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) gives the wife the option for defects in the husband, while Muhammad restricts it to three specific defects and only in the husband.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyar): Option to annul the marriage contract due to a defect.
الجنون (al-junun): Madness, defined as loss of intellect.
الجذام (al-judham): Leprosy, a severe disease from black bile.
البرص (al-barash): Vitiligo, whiteness on skin.
القرن (al-qarn): A bone growth hindering intercourse.
الرتق (al-ratq): Closure of the vagina except for the urinary meatus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the wife has an option to annul the marriage if her husband has madness, leprosy, vitiligo, bone growth, or closure; however, Imam Muhammad limits this to the first three.

Establishing Paternity: Conditional Divorce and Six-Month Minimum
Ruling with proof on paternity from conditional marriage-divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity when a conditional divorce occurs at marriage and explain why the six-month minimum is decisive.

Core Idea
Paternity is established only when birth occurs exactly six months after marriage—the precise intersection of the 'child belongs to the bed' principle and the minimum pregnancy period.

This lesson examines a fascinating scenario where a conditional divorce—one that takes effect upon marriage itself—creates a tight window for paternity. The Hanafi school, known for its caution in establishing lineage, uses the minimum pregnancy period of six months as the key determinant. We will see how the commentary applies two foundational principles to derive the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the fact pattern
Identify the conditional divorce: the man says 'If I marry you, you are divorced.' Then he marries her, so the divorce takes effect immediately at the moment of marriage.
The marriage is valid, but instantly dissolved.
2
Apply the 'child belongs to the bed' principle
The maxim 'al-walad li al-firash' presumes the child of a married woman belongs to the husband. However, here the marriage ended instantly, so we must examine timing carefully.
3
Consider the minimum pregnancy period
The Hanafi school holds that the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months (from conception to birth). If the child is born exactly six months after the marriage, conception must have occurred right at or just after the marriage, i.e., during the brief existence of the marriage.
Six months is counted from the marriage contract, not from cohabitation.
4
Derive the ruling
If born exactly six months after marriage, paternity is established. If born earlier (e.g., 5 months), conception was before marriage—so not his. If born later (e.g., 7 months), conception was after the divorce—so not his.
The ruling is precise: exactly six months, no more, no less.
5
Note the broader maxims
The commentary highlights two principles: (1) lineage is to be established with caution, allowing legal stratagems; (2) the child belongs to the marriage bed. Both guide the outcome.
These principles are foundational across all paternity cases in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النسب والحضانة فصل في ثبوت النسب (من قال : إن نكحتها فهي طالق ، فنكحها ، فولدت لنصف سنة منذ نكحها، لزمه نسبه) قوله : باب النسب والحضانة ; لَمَّا فرغ عن بيان أقسام العدة وما يتعلق بها شرع في بيان ثبوتِ النَّسب وكيفيته، وهو اللازم من اعتدادِ ذوات الأحمال، وضم معه ذكر الحضانة، فإن ثبوت النسب من جانب الأب، والحضانة من جانب الأم، فناسب ضمهما ذكراً. ثمّ النَّسَب - بفتحتين - مصدر ، نسبة إلى أبيه ، وقد يطلق على نفس الارتباط. والحضانة : - بالكسر ، وقيل بالفتح أيضاً - : تربية الولد ، يقال : حضنَ الصبي حضناً وحضانة ، جعله في حضنه أو رباه ، كاحتضنه. [٢] قوله : من قال ... الخ ; اعلم أنَّ هذه المسألة وكذا جميع مسائل النَّسب مبنية على أصلين مؤسسين بالكتاب والسنة : أحدهما : إنّ النسب مما يحتاط في إثباته، فيحتال له ولو بتأويل واستخراج صورة نادرة. وثانيهما : إنّ الولد للفراش، وللعاهر الحجر فاحفظ ذلك. [٣]قوله : منذ نكحها ; أي حين النكاح، يعني وضعت الحمل على رأس ستة أشهر من وقت النكاح ، ولو ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر من حين النكاح لا يثبت نسبه منه، لظهور أنَّ العلوق كان قبل النكاح لا حين النكاح ولا بعده ; إذ لا وضع في أقل من ستة أشهر، ولو ولدته بعد ستة أشهر من ذلك الوقت، ولو كان بزيادة يوم فقط لا يثبت نسبه أيضاً.
Chapter of Lineage and Custody; Section on Establishing Lineage: 'If someone says: If I marry you then you are divorced, then he marries her, and she gives birth at half a year from when he married her, his lineage is established.' His statement: Chapter of Lineage and Custody: When he finished explaining the types of 'iddah and what relates to it, he began explaining the establishment of lineage and its manner, which is necessitated by the 'iddah of pregnant women. And he included with it mention of custody, for establishment of lineage is from the father's side, and custody is from the mother's side, so it was appropriate to include both together. Then, 'nasab' (with two fathas) is a verbal noun meaning lineage to his father, and may be used for the connection itself. And 'hadanah' (with kasrah, and said with fatha as well) means raising a child; it is said: hadana al-sabi hadnan wa hadanah, meaning he placed him in his lap or raised him, like ihtadana. [2] His statement: 'If someone says...' Know that this issue and all issues of lineage are based on two principles established by the Book and Sunnah: One: Lineage is something to be cautious in establishing, so one may resort to trickery to establish it, even if by interpretation and extracting a rare scenario. The second: The child belongs to the marriage bed, and for the fornicator is the stone (i.e., deprivation). So memorize that. [3] His statement: 'From when he married her' i.e., at the time of marriage, meaning she gave birth exactly six months from the time of marriage. And if she gave birth less than six months from the time of marriage, his lineage is not established, because it is clear that conception occurred before marriage, not at or after marriage, since there is no birth in less than six months. And if she gave birth after six months from that time, even if by only one day, his lineage is also not established.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on lineage (nasab) and child custody (hadanah). It begins with a specific ruling: if a man makes a conditional divorce upon marriage ("if I marry you, you are divorced"), then marries the woman, and she gives birth exactly six months after the marriage, the child's lineage is established to him. The commentary explains that the ruling is based on two fundamental principles drawn from the Quran and Sunnah: (1) lineage is to be established with caution, allowing for legal stratagems (hiyal) to attribute a child to the father; (2) the child belongs to the marriage bed (al-walad li al-firash), meaning that a child born to a married woman is attributed to the husband unless proven otherwise. The specific timing of six months is the minimum pregnancy period; if the child is born earlier, it indicates conception before marriage (thus not his), and if born later, it indicates conception after the divorce (since the divorce took effect immediately upon marriage), so the child is not his. The commentary also defines key terms: nasab (lineage) and hadanah (custody).

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; the connection of a child to his father.
حضانة (ḥaḍānah): Custody and upbringing of a child, primarily by the mother.
الولد للفراش (al-walad li al-firāsh): The child belongs to the marriage bed; a legal maxim that attributes a child born in wedlock to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is paternity not established if the child is born more than six months after a conditional marriage-divorce?
A) Because the divorce took effect at marriage, so conception after that is from another man.
B) Because the child must be born within six months to be considered legitimate.
C) Because the marriage was invalid.
D) Because the husband must acknowledge the child.

Key Takeaway
Paternity in a conditional marriage-divorce is established only if the child is born exactly six months after the marriage, due to the interplay of the 'child belongs to the bed' principle and the minimum pregnancy period.

Establishing Lineage with Conditional Divorce at Six Months
Ruling on lineage with conditional divorce, limited to six-month birth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for establishing lineage when a conditional divorce precedes marriage, apply the condition of the six-month birth period, and evaluate the objection regarding the maximum pregnancy period.

Core Idea
Lineage is established only if the child is born exactly six months after marriage – caution requires certainty at the time of marriage.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter on lineage: a man says 'If I marry her, she is divorced' and then marries her. The question is: when is the child's lineage established? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the precise timing of birth relative to the marriage. You will learn why only a six-month birth qualifies, and how the principle of caution (ihtiyat) interacts with the maximum pregnancy period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a conditional divorce preceding marriage. The ruling: if she gives birth exactly six months after the marriage, the child's lineage is established. If less or more, it is not.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'al-waladu lil-firash wa lil-'ahir al-hajar' and the principle that lineage is established with caution are the proofs.
This hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith attributes the child to the marital bed; caution requires certainty of the child's existence at the time of marriage.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
An objection: why not extend lineage establishment up to the maximum pregnancy period of two years? The Hanafi response distinguishes certainty at six months from mere possibility beyond.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If born at 8 months, the Hanafi school does not establish lineage, while the opposing view would establish it up to two years.
Practical consequence for inheritance and custody.

[3] قوله : منذ نكحها ؛ أي حين النكاح، يعني وضعت الحمل على رأس ستة أشهر من وقت النكاح ، ولو ولدته لأقل من ستة أشهر من حين النكاح لا يثبت نسبه منه، لظهور أنَّ العلوق كان قبل النكاح لا حين النكاح ولا بعده ؛ إذ لا وضع في أقل من ستة أشهر، ولو ولدته بعد ستة أشهر من ذلك الوقت، ولو كان بزيادة يوم فقط لا يثبت نسبه أيضاً.

ومهرها) (١) ؛ لأنه لا يبعدُ أنَّ الزوج والزوجة واعترض عليه بأنّ منعهم ثبوت النسب في صورةِ الزيادة في مدةٍ يتصوّر فيها أن يكون الحمل منه، وهو سنتان، وهو أكثر مدة الحمل، ينافي ما قالوا من أنَّ النسب يُحتاط في إثباته، والصورة التي أثبتوا فيها النسب، وهو أن تلد لستة أشهر نادر الوقوع، فإنّه قد تمضي، وهو ردّ لا يسمعُ بولادة ستة أشهر ، مع أن ثبوت النسب في تلك الصورة يحتاج إلى تكلّف بعيد. وأجيب عنه : بأنّ في صورة النصف كان الولد موجوداً وقت النكاح يقيناً، فإذا أمكن حدوثه من العاقـد ولـو بـوجه بعيد تعين ارتكابه بخلاف صورة الزيادة على النصف، فإنّه لم يتيقن فيها بوجوده في وقته، حتى يرتكب له الوجه البعيد.

[1] قوله : ومهرها ؛ أي الكامل، وإن كان الطلاق قبل الوطء ينصفه، وذلك لأنه بثبوت النسب يجعل واطئاً حكماً ، فيكون الطلاق بعد الوطء فيلزم المهر الكامل. فإن قلت : ينبغي وجوب مهرين، مهر بالوطء ومهر بالنكاح ، كما لو تزوج امرأة حال وطئها ، فإنّه يلزمُ فيه مهر مسمى بالنكاح، وعُقر بالوطء. قلت : العقد هناك عارض على الوطء، والدخولُ سابق على النكاح ، فلذلك يجب مهران، ولا كذلك هاهنا، فإنّه يمكن أن يكون الوطء هاهنا حالة التزوج كما ستقف عليه.
