Chapter of Lineage and Custody. Section on Establishing Lineage. Whoever says, 'If I marry her, she is divorced,' then marries her, and she gives birth at half a year from the time of marriage, his lineage is established. [Commentary:] His saying: Chapter of Lineage and Custody: After finishing explaining the categories of waiting period and related matters, he began explaining the establishment of lineage and its modality, which is necessary from the waiting period of pregnant women, and he included with it mention of custody, for lineage is from the father's side and custody from the mother's side, so it was appropriate to include them together. Then lineage is a verbal noun meaning relation to one's father, and it may also be used for the connection itself. Custody, with a kasra and said also with a fatha, is raising a child; one says 'he cared for the child' meaning he placed him in his bosom or raised him. His saying: 'Whoever says...' etc.; know that this issue and all issues of lineage are based on two principles established by the Book and the Sunnah: First, lineage is something to be cautious in establishing, so one seeks stratagems for it even by interpretation and extracting a rare scenario. Second, 'The child belongs to the marriage bed, and for the fornicator is the stone'; so memorize that. His saying: 'from the time of marriage'; i.e., at the time of marriage, meaning she gave birth to the pregnancy at the beginning of six months from the time of marriage. If she gives birth in less than six months from the time of marriage, his lineage is not established, because it is apparent that the conception was before marriage, not at marriage or after, since there is no birth in less than six months. And if she gives birth after six months from that time, even by a day's increase, his lineage is also not established. And her full dowry. [Commentary: because it is not far that the husband and wife...] And an objection was raised against them: that their preventing establishment of lineage in the case of an increase in a period in which it is conceivable that the child is from him—which is two years, the maximum pregnancy period—contradicts what they said that lineage is to be cautious about establishing. And the scenario in which they established lineage, that she gives birth at six months, is rare, for it may pass, and it is a rejected claim, a birth at six months, while establishing lineage in that scenario requires far-fetched interpretation. And it was answered: In the half-year scenario, the child existed at the time of marriage with certainty. So if its occurrence from the contractor is possible, even by a far-fetched method, it is necessary to adopt it, unlike the scenario of increase beyond half a year, for it is not certain that it existed at that time to adopt the far-fetched method. His saying: 'And her dowry'; i.e., the full dowry, even though divorce before consummation halves it, because by the establishment of lineage he is considered a consummator legally, so the divorce occurs after consummation, so the full dowry is necessary. If you say: It should be obligatory to pay two dowries, a dowry for consummation and a dowry for marriage, as if a man marries a woman while actually having intercourse with her, then a named dowry is required for the marriage and a fair amount for intercourse. I say: The contract there is concurrent with intercourse, and entry precedes the marriage, so two dowries are required. But not here, for here intercourse could have occurred at the time of marriage, as you will understand. His saying: 'because it is not far' etc.; this is a clarification of the reasoning of the issue, such that it repels the objection that came at this point, which is that the establishment of lineage in the child of a married woman depends on establishing intercourse and its possibility through marriage, for illicit intercourse does not establish lineage. In our case, when he suspended divorce on the marriage, then married her, the divorce took place upon the marriage. So intercourse here cannot be imagined except after divorce, and it does not establish lineage, for there is no waiting period without being entered, such that it would make that a revocable return.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on lineage and custody, specifically addressing a scenario where a man makes a conditional divorce statement—'If I marry her, she is divorced'—and then indeed marries her. The ruling: if she gives birth exactly six months after the marriage, the child's lineage is established as his. The commentator explains the underlying principles: (1) lineage is to be established cautiously, so we use legal stratagems even if rare interpretations are needed, and (2) the hadith 'the child belongs to the marriage bed' (الفراش). The commentary then meticulously examines the temporal condition: the child must be born at six months exactly—neither less (which would indicate conception before marriage) nor more (which would indicate conception after the divorce occurred upon marriage, since no valid intercourse can take place after the divorce). The discussion also addresses the full dowry being due because lineage establishes the husband as having consummated the marriage legally. An objection is raised and answered: why not establish lineage for a child born up to two years? The response is that only in the six-month case is the child's existence at the time of marriage certain, making the far-fetched probability acceptable; with longer periods, uncertainty remains.

Key Terms
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or paternity; the legal relationship between a child and his father.
الفراش (al-firash): The marriage bed; a metaphor for a valid marital relationship. The child born to the wife is attributed to the husband.
العاهر (al-'ahir): The fornicator; one who engages in illegitimate sexual relations.
الحضانة (al-hadanah): Custody of a child; the right and duty to raise and care for the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) If the child is born within six months to two years after marriage.
B) If the child is born exactly six months after marriage.
C) If the child is born less than six months after marriage.
D) If the child is born more than six months after marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a conditional divorce is pronounced before marriage, the child's lineage is established only if she gives birth exactly six months after marriage, because only then is the child's existence at the time of marriage certain.

Establishing Paternity in Iddah: The Single Witness Dispute
Expansion of conditions for paternity in iddah with intra-Hanafi dispute on single witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for establishing paternity of a child born during iddah and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the sufficiency of a single midwife's testimony, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for fatwa.

Core Idea
The strength of the marital bed (firash) determines whether a single midwife's testimony suffices for paternity in iddah.

The Hanafi school holds that paternity is normally established through marriage or its remnant (firash). But what happens when a woman in iddah claims a child and her ex-husband denies it? The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah outlines the conditions under which lineage is established and then dives into an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: does a single midwife's testimony suffice, or are two men (or one man and two women) required? The answer hinges on whether the firash of the iddah is considered intact, leading to different evidentiary standards between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify modes of paternity establishment
List the circumstances under which the child's lineage is established without dispute: visible pregnancy before birth, husband's acknowledgment of the pregnancy, complete proof of birth (two men or one man and two women), birth within less than two years, heirs' acknowledgment, or the woman being married. Note that 'complete proof' is a key term.
Visible pregnancy (حبل ظاهر) means signs so clear that any observer is preponderantly certain the woman is pregnant.
2
Understand the concept of firash in iddah
Define firash as the 'marital bed' – a legal bond that obliges attribution of children to the husband. The passage discusses whether this bond continues through iddah. Distinguish between revocable (raj‘i) and irrevocable (ba’in) divorce, as the duration of firash differs.
Al-Sarakhsi restricted the discussion to ba’in divorce, but the author of al-Bahr reconciles: in raj‘i iddah within two years, there is agreement on accepting the midwife’s testimony.
3
Contrast Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's views
Abu Hanifa holds that paternity is not established by a single woman's testimony for the birth itself, because the iddah ends when the woman acknowledges delivery, thus ending the firash. The Sahibayn hold that firash continues throughout iddah, so by qiyas to an ongoing marriage, a single midwife's testimony suffices to specify the child.
The Sahibayn's dalil is qiyas jaliy: asl = marriage, far‘ = iddah, illa = the need to identify the child.
4
Apply the distinction: when is a single midwife accepted by agreement?
The passage notes that in revocable divorce (raj‘i), if the child is born within two years, the midwife's testimony is accepted by agreement because the firash is still intact. Beyond two years, dispute arises. In ba’in divorce, the dispute remains according to al-Sarakhsi.
This shows that the ikhtilaf is not absolute; there is ground for consensus on some facts.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, a woman without visible pregnancy or husband's acknowledgment must produce two male witnesses (or one male and two females) to prove the birth. Under the Sahibayn (mufta bihi), the midwife's word alone suffices. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn due to the strength of the firash analogy.
Even Abu Hanifa accepts a single woman's testimony for specification (ta‘yin) if the birth itself is established by other means.

Source Text

وذكر الزيلعي (٢) أنه لا بد لإثبات تعيين الولد عند إنكاره في جميع الصور ؛ أي فيما إذا ثبت الولادة بالحبل الظاهر، أو باعتراف الزوج به ، أو لقيام الفراش، بجواز أن تكون ولدت ولداً ميتاً ، وأرادت إلزامه ولد غيره.
والحاصل : إن شهادة النساء لا تكون حجّة في تعيين الولد إلا إذا تأيدت بمؤيد من ظهور حبل أو اعتراف منه به ، أو فراش قائم، وأما نفس الولادة فلا تثبت إلا بأحد من الأمور المذكورة عنده.
[٣ قوله : فالحاصل ...الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية»: «إذا ولدت المعتدة ولداً لم يثبت نسبه عند أبي حنيفة له إلا أن يشهد بولادتها رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان إلا أن يكون هناك حبل ظاهر أو اعتراف من قبل الزوج، فيثبت النسب من غير شهادة.
وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد الله : يثبت في الجميع بشهادة امرأة واحدة ؛ لأنَّ الفراش قائم بقيام العدّة ، وهو ملزم للنسب ، والحاجة إلى تعيين الولد أنه منها، فيتعين بشهادتها كما في حال قيام النكاح ولأبي حنيفة : إن العدّة تنقضي بإقرارها وضعَ الحمل ، والمنقضي ليس
Or the husband acknowledged [the pregnancy], or her giving birth was established by complete evidence. That is: the lineage of a child of a woman in iddah is established when she claims his birth and the husband denies it, provided there was a visible pregnancy before birth, or the husband acknowledged the pregnancy, or two men or one man and two women testified to the birth, such that the woman entered a house, etc. In summary: lineage is established upon the existence of any of these: visible pregnancy, husband's acknowledgment, establishment of birth by complete evidence, or the birth occurring within less than two years, or the heirs' acknowledgment, or the woman who brought the child being a married woman. The details of all this will come. (1) The term 'mu'taddah' includes a woman observing iddah from death, from irrevocable divorce, or from revocable divorce. This was stated explicitly by Fakhr al-Islam, Qadi Khan, and others among the commentators of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Sarakhsi restricted it to irrevocable divorce. He said in al-Bahr: The correct view is that in revocable divorce, if she brings [the child] after more than two years, testimony is needed as in irrevocable divorce; otherwise, if less, his lineage is established by the testimony of the midwife by agreement, due to the existence of the marital bed. [1] His saying: 'visible pregnancy' means that the signs of her pregnancy are present such that they cause a preponderance of certainty that she is pregnant for every observer. Thus in al-Nahr, and in al-Siraj: its visibility is that she brings it in less than six months. [2] His saying: 'by entering a house, etc.' – This imagery was needed to refute what is said: How can birth be established by complete evidence, i.e., testimony of two men or one man and two women? Because knowledge of it is not obtained except by being present at the place of birth and looking at the private parts, which is forbidden for men. If they do that, they become sinful and their testimony is not accepted, so testimony in this chapter cannot be imagined except from women. The gist of the refutation: That is possible by a woman entering a house, and they knew beforehand with certain knowledge that there is no one in the house – no women, no men, no animal, nothing – and they sat at the door, and that house has only one door, so they knew of the birth by seeing the child or hearing his crying. Thus it becomes permissible for them to testify to her birth, because testimony is not restricted to direct witnessing; rather, certainty of a matter, even by other means, suffices for its performance and acceptance. (1) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (2:496). [2] – And no one was with her, nor anything in the house, and the two men at the door until she gave birth, so they knew of the birth by seeing the child or hearing his voice. He only restricted 'complete evidence' so that lineage is not established by the testimony of a single woman for birth, contrary to them. The conclusion is that according to Abu Hanifa, if the woman in iddah had a visible pregnancy... [1] His saying: 'by seeing the child' means they saw the child through a crack in the door or by entering the house. [2] His saying: 'so that it is not established' means lineage is not established merely by the testimony of a single woman like the midwife, even if she is upright, regarding her birth when the husband denies that. Yes, the testimony of a single woman suffices for specification in the case of acknowledgment. That is, if the husband acknowledges her birth but denies specification of the child and says: 'She did not give birth to this child,' then specification is established by the midwife's testimony by consensus, and it is not established without her by consensus. Thus in al-Bahr. And al-Zayla'i mentioned that it is necessary for establishing specification of the child when he denies it in all cases – i.e., when birth is established by visible pregnancy, by husband's acknowledgment, or by existence of marital bed – because it is possible that she gave birth to a dead child and wants to impose another's child on him. The conclusion: Women's testimony is not evidence for specification of the child unless supported by a support like visible pregnancy, his acknowledgment, or an existing marital bed. As for the birth itself, it is not established except by one of the mentioned matters according to him. [3] His saying: 'the conclusion...' etc. He said in al-Hidayah: 'If the woman in iddah gives birth to a child, his lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa except by two men or one man and two women testifying to her birth, unless there is visible pregnancy or acknowledgment from the husband; then lineage is established without testimony.' Abu Yusuf and Muhammad – may Allah have mercy on them – said: It is established in all cases by the testimony of a single woman, because the marital bed exists by the existence of the iddah, and it obliges lineage, and the need is for specification of the child that he is from her, so it is specified by her testimony as in the case of an existing marriage. Abu Hanifa's argument: The iddah ends by her acknowledgment of delivery, and what is ended is not...
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an expansion on the rules of establishing paternity (nasab) for a child born to a woman in iddah (waiting period after divorce or death). The author first lists the situations in which lineage is established without dispute: visible pregnancy before birth, husband's acknowledgment of the pregnancy, or complete proof of birth (two male witnesses or one male and two females). The passage then delves into the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning the testimony of a single midwife. The commentator explains that the term 'mu'taddah' includes all types of iddah (death, irrevocable, and revocable divorce). However, al-Sarakhsi restricts it to irrevocable divorce. In revocable divorce, if the birth occurs within less than two years, the midwife's testimony is sufficient by agreement because the marriage bond (firash) is still intact. The passage then justifies how two men can testify to a birth without sin: they wait outside the only door of an empty house and hear the baby's cry or see the child from a crack. Abu Hanifa insists on two men or one man and two women for establishing the birth itself, rejecting a single midwife's testimony. This is because he considers that the iddah (and thus the firash) ends with the woman's own claim of having delivered, so the basis for analogy to marriage is weak. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the firash remains throughout the iddah, so a single midwife's testimony suffices by analogy to an ongoing marriage. The text also distinguishes between establishing the birth (requires complete proof) and specifying the child (single woman's testimony suffices if supported by visible pregnancy, acknowledgment, or firash). This is a practical distinction: if the husband admits a birth occurred but disputes which child, the midwife's word is accepted to identify the newborn. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the gist of Abu Hanifa's argument is that the iddah ends with her acknowledgment, so the firash is no longer operative to relax evidence requirements.

Key Terms
حبل ظاهر (habl zahir): Visible pregnancy: signs of pregnancy clearly apparent to observers, causing a preponderance of certainty that the woman is pregnant.
فراش (firash): Marital bed: the legal bond of marriage or its remnant (iddah) that obliges attribution of children to the husband.
شهادة القابلة (shahadat al-qabilah): Testimony of the midwife: a single woman's testimony regarding the birth of a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does Abu Hanifa NOT require two male witnesses (or one male and two females) to establish paternity of a child born to a woman in iddah?
A) If the child is born within two years of divorce.
B) If there is visible pregnancy or the husband acknowledges the pregnancy.
C) If the woman is in iddah from a revocable divorce.
D) If the midwife is an upright woman.

Key Takeaway
The marital bed (firash) during iddah is strong enough that the Sahibayn's view – accepting a single midwife's testimony – is the relied-upon position, making paternity easier to establish and protecting the child's lineage.

Nikah — Marriage

Establishment of Lineage for a Child Born Six Months into Marriage
Ruling on paternity of a child born six months after marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity of a child born six months after marriage, apply the conditions for establishing lineage, and distinguish the effects of acknowledgment based on the number and probity of witnesses.

Core Idea
A child born six months or more after marriage is attributed to the husband; the marriage bed (firash) establishes lineage unless impossible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the core Hanafi principle of lineage (nasab) based on the marriage bed (firash). The text provides the ruling, the proofs from Quran and hadith, and clarifies how acknowledgment by the husband or his silence establishes the child's lineage. It also addresses the scenario where the husband denies the birth, requiring a single midwife's testimony and potentially li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal scenario? A married woman gives birth at six months. State the Hanafi ruling: lineage is established to the husband. Note the conditions: at least six months from marriage, possibility of consummation.
The child is attributed to the husband unless there is impossibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 2:233 and 46:15 to establish the minimum gestation period, and the hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' (Bukhari, Muslim) as the primary proof. Also the incident of 'Umar and 'Ali.
The Quranic verses combine to show 24 months breastfeeding and 30 months total gestation implies 6 months minimum pregnancy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
From the Quran: the two verses together show that the maximum breastfeeding period is 24 months, and total pregnancy plus weaning is 30 months, so pregnancy alone can be as little as 6 months. From the hadith: the child belongs to the marriage bed; the fornicator gets no lineage.
The Hanafi usul: the combination of two mutlaq texts yields a restricted meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars objected that 6 months is too short; the passage responds that the firash is valid and possibility of consummation is assumed. The Shafi'i school requires actual possibility of intercourse, but still accepts 6 months as minimum.
The Hanafi position is more expansive in preserving lineage.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author supports the ruling with the hadith and Quran, and the practice of the Sahaba (Umar, Ali, Uthman, Ibn Abbas). The mufta bihi is that lineage is established, and denial requires li'an.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق/باب ثبوت النسب والحضانة
ومنكوحة أتت به لستة أشهر، أقر به الزوج، أو سكت. فالذي أقر إن لم يكن ممن تصح شهادته؛ لعدم نصاب الشهادة، أو عدم العدالة، يعتبر إقراره في الإرث في حقه فقط، وإن صح شهادته يثبت نسبه مطلقاً: أي في حق المقرّ، وفي حق غيره.
(ومنكوحة أتت به لستة أشهر): أي من وقت النكاح، أقر به الزوج، أو سكت. حاصله: إن إقرار الورثة قد يعتبر في حق المقر خاصة، وذلك بأن كان إقرار المقرّ يكمل به نصاب الشهادة، بأن كان المقر واحداً أو كان المقران غير عدلين، فلا يكون إقراره حجة على الغير ممن لم يقر، بل يكون المقر له شريكاً للمقر في الإرث في نصيبه. وإن تمت الشهادة عدداً ووصفاً بإقرار الورثة بأن كان الإقرار مما فوق الواحد مع العدالة، يكون الإقرار حجة كاملة يثبت به النسب في حق جميع الورثة وغيرهم، فيكون شريكاً لجميعهم في الإرث وقبض الديون وغير ذلك.
قوله: ومنكوحة؛ بالجر عطف على ما عطف عليه ما قبله؛ أي يثبت نسب ولد منكوحة من زوجها إذا ولدته لستة أشهر من وقت النكاح فأكثر، لا إن ولدته لأقل منه؛ إذ لا حمل أقل منه، فيعلم أنها كانت حاملاً عند النكاح. اعترض عليه: بأنه لا يصح ذلك، وإنما يصح ثبوت النسب إذا ولدت لأكثر من ستة أشهر. وأجيب عنه: بأن الفراش قائم والعلوق في ملكه منصور بأن يتزوجها وهو عليها، فوافق الإنزال النكاح، والنسب يحتاط في إثباته، فيثبت في كل صورة يمكن إثباته ولو بتأويل واحتمال. وقد روي عن عمر الله: أنه رفعت إليه امرأة ولدت لستة أشهر فهم برجمها، فقال علي الله: ليس عليها رجم، قال الله: وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ، وقال: وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَلُهُ ثَلَاثُونَ شَهْرًا. أخرجه ابن أبي حاتم، والبيهقي.
وإن جحد ولادتها يثبت بشهادة امرأة، فيلاعن إن نفاه.
فإن جحد ولادتها يثبت بشهادة امرأة، فيلاعن إن نفاه: أي بعدما ثبت ولادتها بشهادة امرأة نفى الولد: أي قال: ليس مني. وأخرج وكيع وعبد الرزاق عن ابن عباس: أن عثمان أتي بامرأة ولدت في ستة أشهر فأمر برجمها، فقال ابن عباس له: إنها إن تخاصمك بكتاب الله تخصمك، يقول الله في كتابه: وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ، ويقول الله في آية أخرى: وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلَاثُونَ شَهْرًا، فقد حملته ستة أشهر، فهي ترضعه لكم حولين كاملين فخلّى عثمان سبيلها.
قوله: لا يحتاج إلى الإقرار؛ لحديث: الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر. أخرجه البخاري وغيره من أصحاب الصحاح. ومن ثم قالوا: لو تزوج مشرقي بمغربية ولم يعلم وصوله إليها، أو غاب عنها كما نكح من دون خلوة، وولدت لستة أشهر من وقت النكاح يثبت نسبه منه لإمكان وصوله إليها بطريق الكرامة أو استخدام جني وغير ذلك. بخلاف ولد من ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر، وولد زوجة الطفل الذي لا يجامع مع نسبه، فإنه لا يثبت نسبه لعدم إمكان الوطء، وكونه من وطئه. والحاصل: إن النسب لصاحب الفراش مطلقاً، لكن التصور والإمكان شرط. كذا في الفتح.
قوله: فإن جحد؛ أي فإن أنكر الزوج ولادة المنكوحة وقال: لم تلد ولداً، وقالت: ولدت يثبت ولادتها بشهادة امرأة واحدة كالقابلة، ولا يحتاج إلى إقامة الشهادة الكاملة؛ لأن ثبوت النسب هاهنا لقيام الفراش، فلا احتياج إلى الشهادة التامة، ولا ظهور الحبل، ولا إقرار الزوج به، مما ذكر في نسب ولد المعتدة.
قوله: أي قال: ليس مني؛ أي ليس من نطفتي ومائي، فهذا قذف للزوجة بالزنا، فيجب به اللعان على ما مر تفصيله في موضعه.
Book of Divorce / Chapter on Establishing Lineage and Custody. And a married woman who gives birth to him at six months, the husband acknowledges him or remains silent. The one who acknowledged, if he is not among those whose testimony is valid due to lack of the required number for testimony or lack of integrity, his acknowledgment is considered in inheritance only with respect to himself. And if his testimony is valid, his lineage is established absolutely: i.e., with respect to the acknowledging person and with respect to others. (And a married woman who gives birth to him at six months): i.e., from the time of marriage, the husband acknowledges him or remains silent. Its summary: The acknowledgment of the heirs may be considered only with respect to the acknowledger, and that is if the acknowledgment of the acknowledger completes the required number for testimony, such that the acknowledger was one or the two acknowledgers were not upright, then his acknowledgment is not a proof against others who did not acknowledge, but rather the acknowledged person becomes a partner with the acknowledger in inheritance in his share. And if the testimony is complete in number and description by the acknowledgment of the heirs, such that the acknowledgment is more than one with uprightness, then the acknowledgment is a complete proof by which lineage is established with respect to all the heirs and others, so he becomes a partner with all of them in inheritance, receipt of debts, and other things. His statement: 'and a married woman' – in the genitive, as an attribute to what preceded; i.e., the lineage of the child of a married woman from her husband is established if she gives birth to him at six months from the time of marriage or more, not if she gives birth to him at less than that, for there is no pregnancy less than that, so it is known that she was pregnant at the time of marriage. An objection was raised against it: that this is not valid, but rather the establishment of lineage is valid only if she gives birth at more than six months. And it was answered: because the bed (firash) is established and conception in his ownership is supported, such that he married her while he was upon her, so the ejaculation coincided with the marriage, and lineage is given precaution in its establishment, so it is established in every form where it is possible to establish it even by interpretation and probability. And it has been narrated from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that a woman who gave birth at six months was brought to him and he intended to stone her, then 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: There is no stoning for her. Allah said: 'And the mothers shall give suck to their children for two whole years' and He said: 'And his gestation and weaning take thirty months.' It was narrated by Ibn Abi Hatim and al-Bayhaqi. And if he denies her giving birth, it is established by the testimony of a woman, then he performs li'an if he denies him. For if he denies her giving birth, it is established by the testimony of a woman, then he performs li'an if he denies him: i.e., after the birth is established by the testimony of a woman, he denies the child: i.e., he says: he is not from me. And Waki' and 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that 'Uthman was brought a woman who gave birth at six months and he ordered her to be stoned, then Ibn 'Abbas said to him: If she argues with you by the Book of Allah, she will defeat you. Allah says in His Book: 'And the mothers shall give suck to their children for two whole years,' and Allah says in another verse: 'And his gestation and weaning take thirty months,' so she carried him six months, and she is now suckling him for two complete years, so 'Uthman let her go. His statement: 'It does not need acknowledgment' because of the hadith: 'The child belongs to the bed, and the stone is for the fornicator.' It was narrated by al-Bukhari and others among the authors of the Sahih collections. And from this they said: If an Easterner marries a Westerner and his reaching her is not known, or he was absent from her as he married without being alone with her, and she gives birth at six months from the time of marriage, his lineage is established from him due to the possibility of his reaching her by way of a miracle (karama) or by using a jinn, etc. This is contrary to the child of a woman who gives birth at less than six months, and the child of a wife of a boy who does not have intercourse with her lineage, for his lineage is not established due to the impossibility of intercourse and that the child is from his intercourse. The conclusion: lineage belongs to the owner of the bed absolutely, but conception and possibility are conditions. Thus in al-Fath. His statement: 'for if he denies' – i.e., if the husband denies the birth of the married woman and says: she did not give birth to a child, and she says: she gave birth, then her giving birth is established by the testimony of one woman like the midwife, and there is no need to produce complete testimony, because the establishment of lineage here is due to the existence of the bed, so there is no need for complete testimony, nor the appearance of pregnancy, nor the husband's acknowledgment, similar to what was mentioned regarding the lineage of the child of a woman in her waiting period. His statement: 'i.e., he said: he is not from me' – i.e., he is not from my semen and my fluid, so this is an accusation of adultery against the wife, and thus li'an becomes obligatory, as its detail has passed in its place.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the establishment of lineage (nasab) for a child born to a married woman (manquha) six months after the marriage contract. The author first presents the core ruling: if the husband acknowledges the child or remains silent, the child's lineage is established. However, the effect of the acknowledgment depends on the credibility of the acknowledging person. If the acknowledger alone (one person) or two persons without moral probity ('adala) acknowledge, the acknowledgment only binds the acknowledger himself; the child inherits from the acknowledger but not from the other heirs who did not acknowledge. If the acknowledgment comes from multiple upright witnesses, the child's lineage is established against all, making him a full heir. The passage then clarifies that 'six months' means from the time of the marriage contract. If the birth occurs at exactly six months or more, the child is attributed to the husband. If less than six months, it is impossible for the child to be from the husband, so lineage is not established. The author addresses an objection: some say lineage is only established if birth occurs after six months (i.e., at more than six). The response relies on the principle of the bed (firash): since the marriage is valid and consummation is possible, the child is presumed legitimate. The proof is the famous hadith 'al-walad lil-firash' (the child belongs to the bed) and the Quranic verses showing that the minimum period of gestation plus breastfeeding is thirty months: two years of breastfeeding (24 months) leaves six months for gestation. This is supported by the incident of 'Umar and 'Ali, and later 'Uthman and Ibn 'Abbas. The passage further states that if the husband denies the birth itself, the birth can be established by the testimony of a single woman (e.g., a midwife). If the husband then denies paternity (qadhf), he must undergo li'an (mutual imprecation). The ruling is based on the principle of precaution in establishing lineage and the strength of the marriage bed. The author also notes extreme possibilities: even if the husband was far away, the possibility of miraculous or jinn-assisted intercourse is considered, highlighting the Hanafi tendency to preserve lineage whenever possible. However, if there is no possibility of intercourse at all (e.g., husband is a minor or birth less than six months), lineage is not established. The key term 'firash' means the valid marriage bed; any child born to a married woman is attributed to the husband unless excluded by li'an or impossibility. The Hanafi school adopts this position as part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
فراش (firāsh): The valid marriage bed; the husband's rights and obligations that make him the presumptive father of any child born to his wife.
لعان (liʿān): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery without witnesses; it results in separation and negation of lineage.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment of the child by the husband; can be explicit or by silence after knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a married woman gives birth to a child exactly six months after the marriage contract, and the husband does not acknowledge the child, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The child's lineage is not established unless the husband acknowledges.
B) The child's lineage is established because the bed (firash) is valid, and the husband must either acknowledge or perform li'an if he denies.
C) The child is considered illegitimate because six months is insufficient time for a viable pregnancy.
D) The child's lineage is established only if the mother testifies with two male witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presumes lineage from the marriage bed; a child born six months or more after marriage is attributed to the husband, and denial must be through li'an.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Maximum Duration of Pregnancy: Two Years
Inter-madhhab dispute over maximum gestation period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the maximum duration of pregnancy, explain the evidence from the hadith of Aisha, and evaluate the Shafi‘i counter-evidence and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The maximum pregnancy is two years — based on a Companion’s statement treated as prophetic teaching, not conjecture.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over the maximum duration of human pregnancy. While modern medicine may suggest shorter durations, Islamic law—particularly the Hanafi school—relies on transmitted evidence from the Prophet (saw) via a saying of Aisha (ra). Other schools, such as the Shafi‘i, extend the period to four years based on rare historical anecdotes. By examining the proofs and responses, you will understand how the Hanafi school defends its two‑year limit and how this dispute affects real rulings on iddah, paternity, and inheritance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years. Note that all three major Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this.
The position is a factual determination, not a hukm taklifi.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognise that al-Shafi‘i holds a maximum of four years, Layth ibn Sa‘d three years, and al-Zuhri seven years. Focus on the Shafi‘i view as the main opponent.
The text names these positions explicitly.
3
Follow the opponent’s proof
Al-Shafi‘i cites two historical reports: al-Dahhak and ‘Abd al-‘Aziz who reportedly were born after four years, and the story of a man absent for two years whose wife gave birth to a child with teeth, leading ‘Umar to accept paternity.
These are the key counter-evidence pieces.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school refutes the reports as unverifiable (only the individuals themselves knew) and explains the long gestation as possible due to illness (closure of the uterus). The story of ‘Umar is reinterpreted: the absence was close to two years, and lineage was established by the husband’s acknowledgment.
The responses are based on critical evaluation of the narrations and legal principles.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference directly affects rulings on iddah (waiting period after divorce/death), paternity, and inheritance. A Hanafi judge will set a two‑year cap, while a Shafi‘i judge may accept up to four years.
This shows how the dispute is not merely theoretical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثر مدة الحمل سنتان
[١]قوله : سنتان ؛ الأصلُ في هذا الباب قول عائشة رضي الله عنها : «ما تزيدُ المرأة في الحمل على سنتين، قدر ما يتحوّل ظلّ عمودِ المغزل)، وفي رواية: «لا تزيد المرأة في حملها على سنتين قدر ظلّ الغزل ) ، أخرجه البيهقي والدارقطني. ومن المعلوم أن قول الصحابي فيما لا يعقل بالرأي ، لا سيما المقادير والمدد محمول على السماع عن النبي ، قال السيد الشريف علي الجرجاني في «شرح الفرائض السراجية»: أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان عند أبي حنيفة وأصحابه ، وعند ليث بن سعد ثلاث سنين، وعند الشافعي له أربع سنين ، وعند الزهري له سبع سنين. لنا : حديث عائشة رضي الله عنها ، فإنّها قالت: «لا يبقى الولد في رحم أمه أكثر من سنتين ولو بظل مغزل»، ومثل هذا لا يعرف قياساً بل سماعاً. وللشافعي ه ما روى أن الضحاك ولد لأربع سنين ، وقد نبتت ثناياه وهـو يضحك، فسمّى ضحاكاً، وأنّ عبد العزيز الماجشوني أيضاً ولد لأربع سنين. وروي أن رجلاً غاب عن امرأته سنتين ، ثمّ قدم وهي حامل ، فهم عمر ه أن يرجمها، فقال له معاذ : وإن كان لك سبيلُ عليها فلا سبيل لك على ما في بطنها ، فتركها حتى ولدت ولداً وقد نبت ثناياه ، وشبه أباه ، فقال الرجل : هذا ابني وربّ الكعبة، فأثبت عمر نسبه وقال : لولا معاذ الله له لهلك عمر والجواب عن الأوّل : إنّ الضحاك وعبد العزيز الله كانا يعرفان ذلك من أنفسهما ولا عرفه غيرهما ؛ إذ لا اطلاع لأحدٍ على ما في الرحم سوى الله الله، ويجوز أن يكون لانسداد فم الرحم لمرض ، فلا اعتداد به.
وعن الثاني : إنّ المراد غيبته عنها قريباً من سنتين ، وإثبات النسب كان بإقرار الزوج.
And the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years. [1] His statement: two years; the basis in this chapter is the saying of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'The woman does not exceed in pregnancy two years, the extent of the shifting of the shadow of a spindle's peg,' and in another narration: 'The woman does not exceed in her pregnancy two years, the extent of the shadow of a spindle.' al-Bayhaqi and al-Daraqutni recorded it. And it is known that the saying of a Companion in matters not based on opinion, especially quantities and durations, is carried on hearing from the Prophet. Sayyid al-Sharif Ali al-Jurjani said in Sharh al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyyah: The maximum duration of pregnancy is two years according to Abu Hanifa and his companions. According to Layth ibn Sa'd, three years; according to al-Shafi'i, four years; according to al-Zuhri, seven years. For us: the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, for she said: 'The child does not remain in his mother's womb more than two years, even if by the shadow of a spindle,' and such a thing is not known by analogy but by hearing. And for al-Shafi'i, there is what is narrated that al-Dahhak was born after four years, and his front teeth had grown and he was laughing, so he was named al-Dahhak, and that Abd al-Aziz al-Majishun was also born after four years. And it is narrated that a man was absent from his wife for two years, then he came and she was pregnant, and Umar intended to stone her, but Muadh said to him: 'Even if you have authority over her, you have no authority over what is in her belly,' so he left her until she gave birth to a child whose teeth had grown and resembled his father, and the man said: 'This is my son, by the Lord of the Kaaba,' so Umar established his lineage and said: 'Had it not been for Muadh, Umar would have perished.' The answer to the first is that al-Dahhak and Abd al-Aziz knew that from themselves but no one else knew it, for no one has knowledge of what is in the womb except Allah, and it is possible that there was a closure of the mouth of the uterus due to illness, so it is not considered. The answer to the second is that the intended meaning was that his absence was close to two years, and the establishment of lineage was by the husband's acknowledgment.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling on the maximum duration of pregnancy, which is two years, and presents the evidence and inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling is based on the hadith of Aisha (ra) that a woman's pregnancy does not exceed two years. The commentator notes that such a statement from a Companion regarding matters that cannot be known by opinion (like durations) is considered as heard from the Prophet (saw). Therefore, it is a strong proof. The Hanafi school, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, all agree on two years. Other scholars like Layth ibn Sa'd (three years), al-Shafi'i (four years), and al-Zuhri (seven years) hold longer periods. Al-Shafi'i's evidence includes historical reports of individuals allegedly being born after four years, such as al-Dahhak and Abd al-Aziz, and the story of a man absent for two years whose wife gave birth to a child with teeth. The Hanafi response refutes these: first, only the individuals themselves claimed to know their gestation, which is not verifiable; secondly, the apparent long gestation could be due to a medical condition (closure of the uterus). Regarding the story with Umar (ra), the Hanafi response is that the absence was close to two years, not exactly two, and the lineage was established by the husband's acknowledgment, not by assuming a longer gestation. This dispute has practical implications for issues like iddah, inheritance, and proof of lineage. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is two years.

Key Terms
أكثر مدة الحمل (akthar muddat al-ḥaml): The maximum possible length of pregnancy from conception to birth, according to a given legal school.
قول الصحابي (qawl al-ṣaḥābī): A statement from a Companion of the Prophet (saw) which, in matters not based on personal opinion, is considered as having been heard from the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two years

D) Nine months

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maximum of two years for pregnancy is derived from the hadith of Aisha, treated as prophetic teaching, and this ruling affects iddah, paternity, and inheritance.

Mother's Right to Custody: Priority Without Compulsion
Opening ruling on custody: mother has priority, not forced

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the mother has priority in custody without being forced, and identify the hadith evidence supporting this.

Core Idea
The mother's right to custody is primary but not compulsory; she may decline unless the child has no other guardian.

This lesson covers the opening ruling of the chapter on custody (hadanah). The law establishes that the natural mother has the strongest claim to raise her young child, but she is not coerced into this duty. The proof is a prophetic hadith that grants her priority over the father as long as she does not remarry. Understanding this balance between right and obligation is essential for applying family law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'والحضانة للأم بلا جبرها'. The ruling is that custody belongs to the mother, and she is not compelled to take it. This is the main legal principle.
The word 'بلا جبرها' means without compulsion upon her.
2
Understand the scope
The phrase 'طلقت أو لا' indicates that this ruling applies whether she is divorced or still married. The mother's right is not affected by marital status.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites the hadith: 'أنت أحق به ما لم تنكحي' (You have more right to him as long as you do not marry). This is from a sahih hadith. It establishes the mother's priority and sets remarriage as the condition that ends her right.
The hadith is narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Hakim, and al-Bayhaqi.
4
Note the exception to non-compulsion
Although the mother is not forced, the commentary adds: if there is no other suitable guardian for the child, she may be compelled to take custody. This protects the child's welfare.
This is from al-Nihayah: 'إذا لم يكن للولد حاضنة سواها تجبر عليها'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الحضانة
والحضانة للأم بلا جبرها طلقت أو لا
[١] قوله : والحضانة للأم؛ هو - بفتح الحاء وكسرها –؛ أي حق تربية الولد حال بقاء النكاح بين أبويه، وحال حصول الافتراق بينهما بطلاق أو موت ثابت للأم - أي النسبية -، فإنَّ الأم الرضاعية لا حق لها في هذا الباب. والأصل فيه حديث: إن امرأة قالت: يا رسول الله إن ابني هذا، بطني له وعاء، وثديي له سقاء، وإن أباه طلقني، وأراد أن ينزعه مني، فقال: «أنت أحق به ما لم تنكحي»، أخرجه أحمد وأبو داود والحاكم والبيهقي من حديث عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص، والوجه فيه أن الأم أشفق وأرعى للولد من الأب؛ ولذا قدمت قراباتها من قراباته.
[٢] قوله : بلا جبرها؛ أي لا تجبر الأم على الحضانة إن أبت منها؛ لأنها عست أن تكون عاجزة عنها، نعم إذا لم يكن للولد حاضنة سواها تجبر عليها؛ لئلا يفوت حق الولد. كذا في «النهاية».
[٣] قوله : طلقت أولاً؛ أي حق التربية ثابت لا حال قيام النكاح وبعد الفرقة كليهما.
(۱) تثبت الحضانة للأم النسبية ولو كتابية أو مجوسية أو بعد الفرقة إلا أن تكون مرتدة حتى تسلم؛ لأنها تحبس أو فاجرة فجورا يضيع الولد به كزنا وغناء وسرقة أو غير مأمونة بأن تخرج كل وقت وتترك الولد ضائعاً وتمامه في الإبانة عن أخذ الأجرة على الحضانة لابن عابدين (١: ٢٤٢). (۲) في سنن البيهقي الكبير (۸): (٤) ، و(سنن الدارقطني (۳) : (٣٠٤)، و(سنن أبي داود» (۲ : ۲۸۳)، و(مسند أحمد (۲) : (۱۸۲) ، ومكارم الأخلاق» (ص ۷۸)، قال الحاكم: صحيح الإسناد. ينظر : خلاصة البدر المنير (٢ : ٢٥٧).
Chapter on Custody. Custody belongs to the mother without compulsion upon her, whether she is divorced or not. [Commentary: Custody is the right to raise the child; it is established for the mother - meaning the natural mother, not the foster mother. The basis is the hadith that a woman said: O Messenger of God, this son of mine, my belly was a container for him, my breasts a water-skin for him, and his father divorced me and wants to take him from me. He said: 'You have more right to him as long as you do not marry.' The reasoning is that the mother is more compassionate. 'Without compulsion' means she is not forced to take custody if she refuses, but if there is no one else, she is compelled. 'Divorced or not' means the right is established both during marriage and after separation.]
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on custody (hadanah) in Hanafi fiqh. The ruling states that the mother has the primary right to custody of her child, and she is not forced to take custody if she does not want to. However, if no other suitable person is available, she may be compelled for the child's welfare. The ruling applies whether she is still married to the father or divorced. The commentary explains that custody (by opening the letter ha) means the right to raise and care for the child. This right is for the natural (nasabi) mother, not the foster (rada'i) mother. The proof is the well-known hadith where the Prophet ﷺ granted a divorced mother priority over the father as long as she does not remarry. The wisdom is that mothers are more compassionate and nurturing. The footnote adds that the right holds even if the mother is a non-Muslim (Kitabiyya or Majusiyya), except if she is an apostate, or if she is immoral in a way that harms the child (e.g., prostitution, drunkenness, theft), or if she is unreliable and leaves the child unattended. In such cases, custody may be transferred.

Key Terms
حضانة (haḍāna): The right to physically raise and care for a child during the years of dependency.
أم نسبية (umm nasabiyya): The biological mother, whose lineage to the child is established through birth.
جبر (jabr): Compulsion; forcing someone to do something against their will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, what terminates the mother's right to custody?
A) Divorce from the father.
B) Remarriage of the mother.
C) The child reaching the age of discretion.
D) The father's request for custody.

Key Takeaway
The mother's custody is a right she may exercise or decline, but it becomes a duty if no other suitable guardian exists, and it is lost upon remarriage or unfitness.

Conditions and Exceptions to Mother's Custody
Conditions and exceptions to mother's custody right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions that invalidate the mother's right to custody according to Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A mother's custody right is conditional on her being the natural mother, not remarried, trustworthy, and not an apostate.

This lesson delves into the details of when a mother loses or retains her right to custody. While the general rule gives her priority, specific conditions and disqualifications are outlined in the commentary and footnotes. Understanding these limitations ensures correct application of family law.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions for custody
From the text, identify the prerequisites: mother must be the natural (nasabi) mother. Foster mother has no right. Also, the right exists whether married or divorced.
The text explicitly says: 'للأم - أي النسبية - فإن الأم الرضاعية لا حق لها'.
2
Identify disqualifications from the hadith
The hadith states: 'ما لم تنكحي' — as long as she does not marry. Remarriage is the primary disqualifier.
This is a condition mentioned in the dalil.
3
Extract disqualifications from the footnote
The footnote adds: apostasy (until she returns to Islam), immorality that harms the child (like zina, singing, theft), and being unreliable (leaving child unattended).
The footnote says: 'إلا أن تكون مرتدة... أو فاجرة... أو غير مأمونة'.
4
Apply the exception to non-compulsion
Even if she qualifies, she is not forced unless no other guardian exists. This interaction shows how the right is balanced.

Ruling on Giving a Child Choice in Custody
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on giving child choice between parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving a young child choice in custody and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of the Prophet giving a child choice.

Core Idea
A young child lacks discernment; giving him choice is harmful, not beneficial.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether a young child should be given the choice to choose between parents after divorce. The Hanafi school holds that a child who has not reached the age of discernment (tamyiz) should not be given such a choice, as he may choose based on immediate whims rather than long-term welfare. We will explore the Hanafi proof from the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and the hadith 'Do not separate a mother from her child,' and see how the Hanafis respond to the Shafi'i reliance on a different hadith where the Prophet gave a child choice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its rationale
Identify the Hanafi ruling: a young child is not given choice in custody because he has not reached the level of discernment to choose what is beneficial. Giving him choice is futile and harmful, as he may choose a more harmful option.
The key concept is the child's lack of tamyiz (discernment).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
The Shafi'i school holds that a discerning child (mumayyiz) may be given a choice, based on a hadith where the Prophet gave a child choice between his mother and father, and the child chose his mother after the Prophet's supplication.
This hadith is reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and others.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis argue that the Prophet's case is specific because his supplication guided the child to the beneficial choice. Therefore, it cannot be generalized by qiyas (analogy) to all children.
The Hanafi response focuses on the unique divine guidance in that case.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi fiqh, the mother retains custody of a young child without giving the child a choice. In Shafi'i fiqh, a discerning child may be given a choice between parents.
This affects court rulings in Hanafi vs. Shafi'i jurisdictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُخَيْرُ طفل ( ولا يُخيرُ طفل ) : خلافا للشَّافِعِي أي يعلم الناس الحيل ؛ لإبطال الأحكام الشرعية ، وارتكاب الأمور المنهية، كالذي يفتي الناس بحل الربا بحيلة الرهن ،وغيرها، ويفتي بحل مطلقة الثلاث من غير تحليل بحيلة ارتداد أحد الزوجين ، ويفتي بحل الزنا وبسماع المزامير عند الغناء بحيلة، وبالجملة: فمن كانت هذه طريقته فهو غير مأمون. (۱) قوله : ولا يخير طفل ؛ لأنه لم يبلغ مبلغاً يختار فيه ما هو أنفع له، فيكون تخييره لغـوا بـل مضراً إذا لم يختر مرافقة من هو أنفع له وأشفق من والديه، بل اختار لسوء فهمه ونقص عقله من مرافقة أضر به ؛ ولهذا لما تنازع عمر بن الخطاب له المطلقة في طفل له فوَّض أبو بكر الصديق الولد إلى الأم، ولم يثبت أنه خيره ، وقال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: «لا تُوله والدة عن ولدها(۳)، أخرجه مالك وزوجته والبيهقي. [٢] قوله : خلافاً للشافعي له ، له ما ثبت عن النبي أنه خير طفلاً بين أمه وأبيه، وقال: «اذهب إلى أيهما شئت، وقال: اللهم اهده، فاختار أمه» (٤) ، أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة، وغيرهم. وأجاب عنه أصحابنا بأن دعاءه قد وفقه لاختيار الانظر الأرفق ، فلا يقاس عليه غيره.
And a young child is not given choice (a young child is not given choice): contrary to al-Shafi'i. That is, he teaches people legal tricks to nullify Islamic rulings and commit prohibited matters, like one who gives fatwa permitting riba through the trick of pawn, etc., and gives fatwa permitting a thrice-divorced woman without lawful dissolution through the trick of apostasy of one spouse, and gives fatwa permitting zina and listening to flutes at singing through a trick. In short: whoever has such a way is not trustworthy. (1) His statement: 'and a young child is not given choice' because he has not reached a level where he can choose what is most beneficial for him. So giving him choice is futile, rather harmful if he does not choose the company of one more beneficial and compassionate than his parents, but chooses due to poor understanding and deficient intellect the company of one more harmful to him. Hence when 'Umar ibn al-Khattab disputed with his divorced wife regarding a child, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq entrusted the child to the mother, and it is not established that he gave the child choice. He said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Do not separate a mother from her child.' Reported by Malik and al-Bayhaqi. (2) His statement: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – he has what is established from the Prophet that he gave a child choice between his mother and father, saying: 'Go to whichever you wish,' and said: 'O Allah, guide him,' so he chose his mother. Reported by the authors of the four Sunan and others. Our companions answered that his supplication guided him to choose the more beneficial option, so others cannot be analogized to him.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a young child should be given the choice to choose which parent to reside with after divorce. The commentator first explains the matn's statement 'a young child is not given choice' by clarifying that this refers to a child who has not reached discernment (tamyiz). The Hanafi position is that giving such a child choice is not merely futile but harmful, as the child may choose based on immediate whims rather than long-term benefit. The commentator supports this with the precedent of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, who did not give a child choice but entrusted him to the mother, and quotes the hadith 'Do not separate a mother from her child.' The opposing Shafi'i position relies on a hadith where the Prophet gave a child choice between his parents, and the child chose his mother after the Prophet's supplication. The Hanafi response is that this case is unique because the Prophet's supplication guided the child to the correct choice, so it cannot be used as a general precedent. Thus, the Hanafi school maintains that a child below the age of discernment is not to be given choice in custody matters.

Key Terms
تخيير (takhyeer): Giving a child the option to choose between parents in custody.
طفل (tifl): A young child who has not reached the age of discernment (tamyiz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a young child not given a choice between parents in custody?
A) Because the child is too young to understand.
B) Because the child may choose harm over benefit due to lack of discernment.
C) Because the mother always has priority regardless of choice.
D) Because the father is the natural guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school upholds that a young child is not to be given choice in custody because his lack of discernment leads to potential harm; the Shafi'i proof from the Prophet's hadith is limited to that unique case.

Duration of Mother's Custody: Independence vs. Fixed Age
Ruling on the period of custody for mother and grandmother of a son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that ends the mother's right to custody and explain why the seven-year estimate is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Custody ends when the child is independent; the seven-year age is a later scholarly estimation, not from the primary texts.

The Hanafi school has a nuanced position on when a mother's right to custody terminates. While the primary transmitted texts (zahir al-riwayah) set no fixed age and instead make it contingent on the child's ability to perform basic tasks independently, later scholars introduced a practical guideline. In this lesson, we examine the source text and its commentary to understand the legal reasoning behind the seven-year estimate and its status as the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger for custody termination
The mother's right to custody ends when the child can eat, drink, dress, and clean himself independently. This is the core condition from the matn.
The commentator clarifies that 'independently' (wahdahu) applies to all these actions.
2
Understand the zahir al-riwayah position
In the core transmitted texts, no specific age is set. The ruling is left absolute because the age of independence varies among children.
This is a hallmark of Hanafi methodology: allowing flexibility based on circumstances.
3
Examine the later estimation by Al-Khassaf
Al-Khassaf estimated the age as seven years, based on the general norm and supported by the hadith about commanding prayer at seven. This became the mufta bihi.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Bakr al-Razi estimated nine years, but the fatwa is on seven.
4
Consider the optional issue of takhyeer (choice)
The passage mentions reports suggesting the child may choose. The commentator restricts this to cases where the child is presumed to choose the more beneficial option.
This is a secondary point; the main ruling is based on independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والأم والجدة أحق بالابن حتى يأكل ويشرب ويلبس ويستنجي وحده : قَدَّرهُ الحَصافُ الله بسبع سنين ، وعليه الفتوى). ويشكل عليه أنه قد ثبت التخيير عن أبي هريرة له عند ابن حبان ، وعن عمر عند عبد الرزاق ، وعن علي الله عند الشافعي ، ولعلّ الحق هو القولُ بجواز التخيير لكن لا مطلقاً، بل بشرط أن يكون المظنون اختيار الطفل الأرفق الانظر وإلا فلا. [١] قوله : والأم....الخ ؛ شروع في بيان مدة الحضانة، وهي مختلفة باختلاف الذكرِ والأنثى، وظاهرُ كلامه يحكم بأنّ المدة المذكورة لحضانة الذكر مختصة بما إذا كانت الحاضنة أماً أو جدة لأب أو لأم وليس كذلك، بل هذه المدة في كل حاضنة، صرّح به «الدر المختار» وغيره، وإنما التفرقة ما إذا كانت الحاضنة إما أو جدة، وبين ما إذا كانت غيرهما في حضانة الأنثى. [٢] قوله : وحده ؛ قيد لجميع الأفعال المذكورة، والحاصل : إنّ الحضانة للصغير غايتها أن يستغني عن خدمةِ النِّساء، فإن بعد ذلك لا يحتاج إلى كونه معهن، بل إلى التأديب والتعليم، والرجال أحقاء به، وذلك إنما يعرف بأن يقدر على أن يأكل وحده ويشرب ويلبس وينام ويستنجي. وبالجملة : يقدر على أن يفعل هذه الأفعال ونحوها من غير معين، بأن يبلغ سنّاً يقدر فيه الصبي غالباً على هذه الأفعال ولا يقدح فيه عدم قدرة صبي عليها لمرض. [٣] قوله : قدره ؛ يشير إلى أنّ في ظاهر الرواية لم يقدّر سن توجد فيه هذه الغاية، بل ترك الحكم مطلقاً، بناءً على أنّ القدرة على هذه الأفعال، والاستغناء عن النِّساءِ يختلف وجوده بحسب اختلاف طبائع الصبيان. والخصاف له قدره بسبع سنين ، واعتمد عليه المشايخ ؛ نظراً إلى أن الغالب في هذا السن هو القدرة، ويؤخذ ذلك من حديث: مروا صبيانكم بالصلاة إذا بلغوا (۱) وقدره أبو بكر الرازي بتسع سنين، والفتوى على قول الخصاف كما في غرر الأحكام»(۱) : ٤١١)، و (شرح ملا مسكين (۱۳۱) ، و(الدر المنتقى (١ : ٤٨٢)، وغيرها.
His statement: 'And the mother and grandmother are more entitled to the son until he eats, drinks, dresses, and cleans himself independently.' Al-Khassaf estimated it as seven years, and upon it is the fatwa. And it is problematic that choice (takhyeer) has been established from Abu Hurairah as reported by Ibn Hibban, and from 'Umar as reported by 'Abd al-Razzaq, and from 'Ali as reported by al-Shafi'i. Perhaps the truth is the opinion permissibility of choice, but not absolutely, rather with the condition that it is presumed the child will choose the more beneficial option; otherwise not. [1] His statement: 'And the mother...' is the beginning of explaining the duration of custody, and it differs according to male and female. The apparent meaning of his words rules that the mentioned period for custody of a male is specific to when the custodian is a mother or grandmother, but it is not so; rather this period applies to every custodian, as stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others. The difference is only between when the custodian is a mother or grandmother, and when it is someone else, in the custody of a female. [2] His statement: 'independently' is a condition for all the mentioned actions. The summary: custody of a young child ends when he becomes independent of women's service; after that he does not need to be with them, but rather needs discipline and education, and men are more suited for that. That is known by his ability to eat alone, drink, dress, sleep, and clean himself. In short: he can do these and similar actions without assistance, by reaching an age at which a boy is generally capable of these actions, and it is not harmed by a boy's inability due to illness. [3] His statement: 'estimated' indicates that in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) no specific age was fixed for this goal, rather the ruling was left absolute, based on the fact that ability for these actions and independence from women varies according to the natures of boys. Al-Khassaf estimated it as seven years, and the later scholars (mashayikh) relied on it, considering that generally at this age ability exists, and it is taken from the hadith: 'Command your children to pray when they reach seven.' And Abu Bakr al-Razi estimated it as nine years, but the fatwa is on the statement of al-Khassaf as in Ghurar al-Ahkam, Sharh Mulla Miskin, al-Durr al-Muntaqa, etc.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage explains the duration of custody (hadanah) for a male child. The matn states that the mother and grandmother have a stronger right to the son until he can eat, drink, dress, and clean himself independently. The commentator clarifies that this period applies to any custodian, not just mother/grandmother. The end of custody is determined by the child's independence from female service; he then needs male supervision for discipline and education. The commentator notes that in the zahir al-riwayah (the core transmitted texts), no fixed age was set; rather it was left to the child's actual ability, which varies. However, Al-Khassaf estimated the age as seven years, and this was adopted by later scholars (mashayikh) as the relied-upon view, supported by the hadith about commanding prayer at seven. There is also an opinion of Abu Bakr al-Razi estimating nine years, but the fatwa is on seven. The passage also mentions a problematic issue regarding takhyeer (giving choice) reported from some companions, but the commentator suggests that choice may be permissible with the condition that the child is likely to choose the more beneficial option.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): Custody and physical care of a young child.
الخصاف (al-Khassaf): The Hanafi jurist Abu Bakr al-Khassaf (d. 261/874) who estimated the age of custody termination at seven years.
تخيير (takhyeer): Giving the child a choice between parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the son reaches puberty.
B) At seven years, as estimated by Al-Khassaf.
C) At nine years, as estimated by Abu Bakr al-Razi.
D) When the son demands to live with his father.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines the end of mother's custody by the child's independence, with seven years as a practical guideline.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Judicial Separation for Non-Payment of Maintenance
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on tafriq due to inability to pay nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tafriq due to non-payment of nafaqah, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, poverty does not justify judicial separation unless extreme need forces a Shafi'i deputy's intervention.

This passage addresses a critical ikhtilaf (dispute) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: can a qadi separate a married couple when the husband cannot pay maintenance? The Hanafis, led by Abu Hanifa, maintain that the loss of wealth is not as grave as the loss of procreation, so separation is not the default. However, they recognize a necessity exception through istihsan. Let us walk through the proofs and responses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the exact legal question at hand? The passage opens with the Hanafi recognition of necessity (darurah) for separation, but immediately qualifies it.
The question: Should a qadi separate a couple when the husband cannot pay nafaqah?
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis do not permit direct separation by a Hanafi qadi. Instead, they allow a procedure: the qadi appoints a Shafi'i deputy to perform the separation (tafriq) if the wife's need cannot be met otherwise.
This is based on istihsan, not direct qiyas.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i cites a hadith: 'Separate between them.' The Hanafis examine this hadith and find it defective (mu'allal).
The hadith is weak according to Ibn Hajar.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the primary purpose of marriage is procreation (tawallud wa tanasul), whereas wealth is secondary. The wife can be protected by ordering the husband to borrow; only when borrowing is impossible does the need justify separation via a Shafi'i deputy.
This is a qiyas khafi reasoning, distinguishing poverty from impotence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? A Hanafi wife cannot obtain a divorce solely for non-payment of maintenance in normal circumstances; a Shafi'i wife can be judicially separated immediately.
The Hanafi judge must not directly separate but may facilitate through a Shafi'i judge if necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأصحابنا له لما شاهدوا الضرورة في التفريق ؛ لأنَّ دفع الحاجةِ الدائمة لا يتيسر بالاستدانة، والظَّاهِرُ أنَّها لا تجد من يقرضُها ، وغِنَى الزوج في المال أمرٌ متوهم استحسنوا " أن ينصب القاضي نائباً شافِعِيُّ المذهب يفرِّقُ بينهما .
والسنة أحد الأمرين :
إما أن يمسكها بمعروف.
وإما أن يسرحها ويطلق عنانها.
وقد عجز بعجزه عن النفقة لإعساره عن الإمساكِ بالمعروف، فيجب عليه أن يسرحها ويفارقها ، وإذ لم يفعله وتضررت المرأةُ قامَ القاضي مقامه ؛ لكونه ذا ولاية عامة، فيفرّق بينهما ، ونظيره التفريق في الزوج العنين والمجبوب.
ونحن نقول : إنما جازَ تفريقه في الجبّ والعِنّة لفوات أصل المقصود من النكاح ، وهو التوالد والتناسل، ولا كذلك المال، فإنّه تابع في النكاح ، فلا يستوجب فوته التفريق ، ويمكن دفع حاجتها الدائمة بأمر للاستقراض عليه، فلا تتضرر المرأة في هذه الصورة كتضررها في الجب والعنّة، حتى يلزم عليه التسريح بإحسان، ويقوم القاضي مقامه.
وقد يستدل الشافعي بحديث أبي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في الرجل لا يجد ما ينفق على امرأته : «يفرق بينهما»، أخرجه الدارقطني والبيهقي، وهذا نص في الباب، فلا يقبل قول مخالف له ، فإن القول ما قال الرسول مع الهلال والا ما قاله غيره مخالفاً لقوله كائناً من كان، لكنه حديث معلول غير ثابت كما حققه الحافظ ابن حجر له في «تلخيص الحبير»، ونقح أنّ الدارقطني وهم في روايته، وتبعه في خطئه البيهقي، نعم روي مثله عن سعيد بن المسيب به موقوفا عليه. وبالجملة : إن ثبت في هذا الباب حديث مرفوع بسند معتمد حاكم بالتفريق فعلى الرأس والعين، وإلا فالقول ما قال أصحابنا ما لم تدعُ إلى التفريق الحاجة بأن لم يتيسر الاستدانة أيضاً.
Our companions, when they saw the necessity for separation because fulfilling the perpetual need cannot be achieved by borrowing, and it is apparent that she will not find anyone to lend to her, and the husband's wealth is a speculative matter, they deemed it good (istihsan) that the judge appoint a Shafi'i deputy to separate between them. The Sunnah is one of two matters: either to retain her honorably, or to release her and let her go. He has become incapable due to his inability to provide maintenance because of his poverty from retaining her honorably, so it is obligatory upon him to release her and separate. If he does not do so and the woman is harmed, the judge stands in his place due to his general authority, so he separates between them. Its analogy is separation in the case of the impotent or castrated husband. We say: separation in the case of castration or impotence is permitted only because the original purpose of marriage—procreation—is lost. Money is not like that, for it is subordinate in marriage, so its loss does not necessitate separation. Her perpetual need can be met by ordering him to borrow, so the woman is not harmed in this case like she is harmed in the case of castration and impotence, such that he is obligated to release her with kindness and the judge takes his place. Al-Shafi'i adduces the hadith of Abu Huraira that the Prophet ﷺ said concerning a man who cannot find what to spend on his wife: 'Separate between them,' reported by al-Darqutni and al-Bayhaqi. This is a clear text in the chapter, so the objection of anyone opposing it is not accepted, for the saying is what the Messenger said, and not what anyone else says contrary to his word, whoever he may be. But this hadith is defective (mu'allal), not established, as al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar confirmed in Talkhis al-Habir, and he determined that al-Darqutni erred in its narration, and al-Bayhaqi followed him in his error. Yes, something similar is narrated from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib as a mawquf. In summary: if a marfu' hadith with a reliable chain of transmission is established in this chapter, ruling for separation, then it is most welcome; otherwise, the saying is that of our companions, unless the need for separation is pressing because borrowing is also not possible.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school concerning whether a husband's inability to pay maintenance (nafaqah) can lead to judicial separation (tafriq). The Hanafi position, supported by istihsan (juristic preference), is that the qadi does not directly order separation. Instead, to avoid severe hardship for the wife, the qadi may appoint a Shafi'i judge to issue the separation. This is analogous to cases of impotence or castration, but with a key difference: the loss of wealth is secondary in marriage, whereas the loss of procreation is primary. The wife's need can be alleviated by ordering the husband to borrow; therefore, the harm to the wife is less acute. The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith: 'Separate between them.' The Hanafis respond by questioning the hadith's authenticity, citing Ibn Hajar's critique that al-Darqutni erred in transmitting it. The Hanafis conclude that if an authentic marfu' hadith is found, they would accept it; otherwise, the Hanafi ruling stands, unless the need is so extreme that borrowing is also impossible.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Maintenance due from husband to wife for food, clothing, lodging, etc., while she is in his custody.
التفريق (al-tafriq): Judicial separation ordered by a qadi between spouses due to a valid cause.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from the ruling of an analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is separation not permitted for a husband's poverty?
A) Because poverty makes the marriage invalid.
B) Because wealth is a secondary purpose of marriage and the wife can ask him to borrow.
C) Because the husband must be imprisoned first.
D) Because the wife must leave the house.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts judicial separation for non-payment of maintenance to extreme necessity, using istihsan to permit it only via a Shafi'i deputy, while the Shafi'i school sees it as an obligation based on a hadith that the Hanafis consider weak.

Maintenance Obligation of a Slave Husband
Ruling on maintenance of a slave husband with three scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for a slave husband's maintenance obligation and apply the Hanafi ruling to each.

Core Idea
A slave husband owes maintenance only when his wife is free; otherwise, the master bears it.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced Hanafi ruling on nafaqah (maintenance) when the husband is a slave. The passage clarifies that the slave's liability depends entirely on the legal status of the wife and her relationship to the master. We will explore the three distinct situations presented, understanding the conditions that shift the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The passage states that the phrase 'upon him' means maintenance is wajib on the slave husband himself, not on his master. This applies when the wife is free.
This is the default ruling: the husband, even if a slave, is personally liable for his free wife's maintenance.
2
Recognize the exception for a same-master slave wife
If the wife is also a slave and belongs to the same master as the husband, then the husband owes no maintenance. The master is responsible because he owns both slaves and must maintain them.
Here, the master's ownership overrides the husband's marital obligation.
3
Understand the conditional scenario for a different-master slave wife
If the wife is a slave of a different master, the husband is not liable unless her master gives her to the husband (i.e., allows her to live with him) and does not employ her for his own service. If the master employs her, the husband's liability is nullified, and the master retains responsibility.
The key condition is the wife's master 'bawwa'aha' (provides her) and 'lam yastakhdimha' (does not employ her).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : عليه ؛ أي واجبة ولازمة على القِنّ لا على مولاه، وهذا إذا كانت الزوجة حرّة ، فإنّه تجب عليها نفقتها ، وأما إذا كانت زوجة القنّ أمة ، فإن كانت أمة لمولاه فلا تجب نفقتها على الزوج ؛ لأنهما جميعاً ملك المولى، ونفقة المملوك على المالك.
وأما إن كانت أمةً لغيره فلا تجب عليه نفقتها إلا إذا بوأها مولاها – أي دفعها إلى الزوج - ، ولم يستخدمها وإلا فلا. كذا في «البحر» وغيره.
His statement: 'upon him' means obligatory and binding upon the slave, not upon his master. This is when the wife is free, for maintenance is obligatory upon him. As for when the slave's wife is a slave, if she is a slave of his master, then her maintenance is not obligatory upon the husband, because both are the property of the master, and the maintenance of a slave is upon the owner. But if she is a slave belonging to someone else, her maintenance is not obligatory upon him unless her master provides her to him—i.e., gives her to the husband—and does not employ her; otherwise, not. Thus in 'al-Bahr' and others.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the maintenance obligation of a slave husband. The commentator explains that the phrase 'upon him' indicates that maintenance is binding on the slave himself, not his master, but only when the wife is free. If the wife is also a slave, the ruling bifurcates: if she belongs to the same master as the husband, then no maintenance is due from the husband because both are the master's property, and the master is responsible for his slaves' maintenance. If she belongs to a different master, then maintenance is not due from the husband unless the wife's master gives her to the husband (i.e., allows her to live with him) and does not employ her for his own service. The source cited is 'al-Bahr' (likely al-Bahr al-Ra'iq).

Key Terms
قِنّ (qinn): A slave who is fully owned, as opposed to a mudabbar or mukatab.
بوأها (bawwa'aha): The master provides the female slave to her husband for residence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the wife is a slave of the same master
B) When the wife is free
C) When the wife is a slave of a different master and her master does not employ her
D) Always, because marriage imposes maintenance

Key Takeaway
A slave husband's maintenance obligation depends on the wife's legal status: wajib on him if she is free, otherwise on the master under specific conditions.

Nikah — Marriage
